The Bitter Dichotomy: Analyzing Dualism in Islamic Education
Author analyzes the epistemological crisis caused by dualism in Islamic education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main manifestations of dualism in Islamic education described by the author and trace their consequences.

Core Idea
The crisis is not political but epistemological: two incompatible concepts of knowledge and human personhood collide.

The author describes a deep crisis in Islamic education where the Islamic creed and Western curricula are in conflict, producing a 'bitter dichotomy' that robs the system of legitimacy. In this lesson, we will parse his analysis of the problem, identify its causes and manifestations, and understand why earlier attempts at integration failed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two educational systems
Find the two 'products' the author describes at the start. What are their characteristics? One is Islamic, the other secular.
Note the contrasting phrases: 'ملؤه الإيمان والورع والتقوى' vs. 'يظن أنه وحده قادر على صنع كل شيء بلا حدود...'.
2
Locate the core incompatibility
The author argues that Islamic and Western concepts of the human personality are contradictory. Find that statement and note how each side defines human personhood.
Islamic view: integrated spirit and ethics. Western view: sets aside the spiritual.
3
Define the 'bitter dichotomy'
The passage says 'الانفصام النكد' arises from lack of harmony between creed and curricula. What exactly is out of harmony? The ummah's creed vs. the objectives, content, means, activities, evaluation of curricula.
This is the primary cause.
4
Trace the response and its failure
How did Muslim scholars respond? They confronted dualism but neglected to confront imported secular ideas. What was the result? Cultural dualism between religious scholars and secularists.
They preserved spiritual concepts in a limited sector only.
5
Identify the two reasons for liberalism's resistance
The author gives two reasons why Western liberalism was harder to resist than Marxism. Find them and explain why each made integration difficult.
First: influence on knowledge branches. Second: inability to formulate Islamic alternatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول - أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
أحدهما نتاج نظام تعليم إسلامي ملؤه الإيمان والورع والتقوى. ثانيهما: نتاج أو مخرج نظام تعليم علماني يظن أنه وحده قادر على صنع كل شيء بلا حدود لطاقته ولا حاجة لهداية الله وتوفيقه (۱).
ولذلك فقد خرج المؤتمرون في المؤتمر الأول للتعليم الإسلامي المنعقد بمكة المكرمة بأنه من شبه المستحيل التوفيق بين مفهومين متناقضين عن الشخصية الإنسانية، حيث هي في الإسلام جوانب متكاملة من الروح والأخلاق وأي نشاط إنساني آخر فرديًا كان أم جماعياً في حين أن طرق التدريس الغربية تقوم بتنحية الجانب الروحي للإنسان(٢).
إن عدم الانسجام بين عقيدة الأمة وثقافتها من جهة وبين المناهج بجميع عناصرها من أهداف ومحتوى ووسائل وأنشطة مختلفة وتقويم من جهة أخرى يمثل سببًا رئيسا في بروز مشكلة الانفصام النكد في النظام المعرفي التعليمي في العالم الإسلامي، مما أفقده الشرعية (۳).
وقبالة ذلك الوضع بدأت مجابهة علماء المسلمين – الذين تلقوا تعليـمـا إسلاميا تقليدياً - لفكرة الثنائية، ولكنهم أغفلوا مواجهة الأفكار والمفهومات العلمانية المستوردة، فتمكنوا من الإبقاء على المفهومات الروحية في قطاع محدود قطاعات المجتمع، مما أدى إلى ظهور الازدواجية الثقافية في العالم الإسلامي، بين طبقة علماء الدين أو التعليم الإسلامي، وبين نظام التعليم الحديث الذي أدى إلى خلق طبقة العلمانيين (4) .
وكان من اليسير من وجهة النظر العقائدية البحتة مقاومة الأفكار الماركسية المهيمنة وقتذاك، ولكن كان من الصعوبة بمكان مقاومة آثار الليبرالية الغربية، وذلك لسببين رئيسين:
أحدهما : تأثير التربية الغربية على شتى فروع المعرفة.
ثانيهما: عدم تمكن علماء المسلمين من صياغة المفهومات الإسلامية التي يمكن لها أن تحل محل مثيلاتها الليبرالية (۱).
ومع أن جهودًا بُذلت في سبيل دمج نظامي التعليم الديني والعلماني في نظام واحد من منطلق فكرة أسلمة المنهاج إلا أنه لم يكتب لها النجاح، لأن معالجتها تميزت بالأحادية، ولم تلتفت إلى أبعاد المشكلة وجوانبها المختلفة (٢).
وعلى الرغم مما قد يبدو أنه استقصاء للمشكلة يشير إلى استعصاء الجوانبها يوما بعد آخر؛ إلا أنَّ ثمة مبشرات تفيد بأن ذلك الوضع لن يستمر طويلاً - بإذن الله تعالى - بالاستناد إلى جملة من المعطيات وأبرزها ما يلي:
أولاً : قيام مؤسسات تربوية وتعليمية وأكاديمية عليا داخل العالم الإسلامي وخارجه، على أساس من الإيمان بوحدة المعرفة، وعدم اللجوء إلى الفصل بين معارف الوحي ومعارف الكون. ومن تلك المؤسسات التي تستحق الإشارة هنا - وإن لم تكن جميعها متبناة من قبل الأنظمة السياسية لتلك البلدان، أو أن ثمة فصلاً من نوع آخر بين النظرية والتطبيق – مايلي:
١ - فلسفة التربية في الجمهورية اليمنية، التي تقوم على أساس:
أ - الإيمان بالله ووحدانيته خلق الكون وسخره للإنسان، وفق سنن إلهية دقيقة وثابتة.
(۱) المرجع السابق، ١٣ - ١٤.
(٢) المرجع نفسه، ٣٦.
The second chapter: The first section - Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity
One of them is the product of an Islamic educational system filled with faith, piety, and righteousness. The second is the product or output of a secular educational system that thinks it alone is capable of making everything without limits to its capacity and without need for God's guidance and success (1).
Therefore, the participants in the first conference on Islamic education held in Mecca concluded that it is nearly impossible to reconcile two contradictory concepts of the human personality, as in Islam it is integrated aspects of spirit, ethics, and any other human activity, individual or collective, while Western teaching methods set aside the spiritual aspect of man (2).
The lack of harmony between the creed and culture of the ummah on one hand and the curricula with all their elements—objectives, content, means, various activities, and evaluation—on the other hand represents a primary cause of the emergence of the bitter dichotomy in the cognitive-educational system in the Islamic world, which has deprived it of legitimacy (3).
In response to that situation, Muslim scholars—who received traditional Islamic education—began to confront the idea of dualism, but they neglected to confront imported secular ideas and concepts, so they managed to preserve spiritual concepts in a limited sector of society, leading to the emergence of cultural dualism in the Islamic world between the class of religious scholars or Islamic education and the modern education system, which created a class of secularists (4).
It was easy from a purely doctrinal point of view to resist the dominant Marxist ideas at that time, but it was very difficult to resist the effects of Western liberalism for two main reasons:
First: The influence of Western education on various branches of knowledge.
Second: The inability of Muslim scholars to formulate Islamic concepts that could replace their liberal counterparts (1).
Although efforts were made to integrate the religious and secular education systems into one system based on the idea of Islamization of the curriculum, it did not succeed, because its treatment was characterized by being one-dimensional and did not pay attention to the different dimensions and aspects of the problem (2).
Despite what may appear to be an investigation of the problem indicating the intractability of its aspects day after day, there are glad tidings that this situation will not last long - by God's will - based on a number of data, most notably the following:
First: The establishment of educational, instructional, and higher academic institutions within and outside the Islamic world on the basis of faith in the unity of knowledge and not resorting to separation between revealed knowledge and empirical knowledge. Among those institutions worth mentioning here - even if not all are adopted by the political systems of those countries, or there is a separation of another kind between theory and practice - are the following:
1 - The philosophy of education in the Republic of Yemen, which is based on:
a - Belief in God and His oneness, He created the universe and subjected it to man according to precise and constant divine laws.
(1) Previous reference, pp. 13-14.
(2) Same reference, p. 36.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage diagnoses the epistemological crisis in the Islamic world caused by the clash between Islamic and Western educational systems. The author begins by contrasting two educational products: one from an Islamic system rooted in faith and piety, and another from a secular system that claims self-sufficiency without divine guidance. This sets up the fundamental incompatibility highlighted by the first Islamic education conference in Mecca: Islamic and Western concepts of the human personality are contradictory, as Islam integrates spirit and ethics while Western methods exclude the spiritual realm. The author then identifies the lack of harmony between the ummah's creed and its curricula as the primary cause of a 'bitter dichotomy' in the cognitive-educational system, robbing it of legitimacy. The response of Muslim scholars, though commendable in confronting dualism, failed to address imported secular concepts, leading to cultural dualism between religious scholars and modern-educated secularists. The author notes that resisting Marxism was doctrinally easier, but Western liberalism proved harder to resist due to the pervasive influence of Western education and the inability of Muslim scholars to formulate Islamic alternatives. Efforts to integrate the two systems through Islamization of curricula failed due to a one-dimensional approach. Despite the bleak picture, the author points to hopeful signs, first among them the establishment of institutions based on the unity of knowledge, citing the example of Yemen's educational philosophy grounded in belief in God's oneness and the subjection of the universe to humans under divine laws.

Key Terms
الانفصام النكد
الازدواجية الثقافية
وحدة المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main reason earlier attempts at integrating religious and secular education failed?
A) They were too focused on curricula content
B) They were one-dimensional and did not address all aspects of the problem
C) They were resisted by religious scholars
D) They were abandoned due to lack of funding

Key Takeaway
The crisis in Islamic education stems from a deep conceptual clash between the Islamic view of integrated human personhood and the Western secular view that excludes the spiritual, producing a bitter dichotomy that must be resolved through a unified epistemological framework.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the three key terms from the passage (الانفصام النكد, الازدواجية الثقافية, وحدة المعرفة), write a short paragraph explaining how each contributes to the crisis described.
?
Reflect on an example from your own experience or knowledge: identify a case where an Islamic educational institution struggles with the duality between Islamic values and modern academic standards. Apply the author's analysis to explain why integration is difficult.

Unity of Knowledge: Integrating Religious and Secular Sciences
Author discusses unity of knowledge and integration of sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the Islamic concept of wahdat al-ma'rifa and explain its practical implications for education as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
All knowledge is one because its ultimate source is one: Allah.

This passage from a modern Islamic educational critique argues that religious questions about existence and destiny are deeply human and deserve serious study. The author proposes a concrete plan to integrate religious and secular sciences, rooted in the Quranic principle that all revelation comes from one God. Understanding this unity challenges the false dichotomy between 'sacred' and 'secular' knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem: false dichotomy
Notice how the author states that even if religious answers were wrong, the questions themselves remain valid. The mistake is to dismiss religious inquiry altogether.
2
Extract the Quranic foundation for unity
The author cites verses commanding belief in all scriptures and messengers, e.g., Al-Baqara 2:285, which emphasizes 'we make no distinction between any of His messengers.' This establishes that all revealed knowledge shares one source.
Focus on the phrase 'لا نفرق بين أحد من رسله'.
3
Understand the proposed integration method
The author suggests two groups: secular specialists study religious principles, and religious specialists study secular basics. This is a practical two-way integration for education.
Note the emphasis on early-stage religious education (first three stages).
4
Articulate the unifying principle
The passage concludes that 'unity of knowledge includes the universal principles of education.' The underlying principle is tawhid: the oneness of God as source of all truth.
This is the core of wahdat al-ma'rifa.

الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول- أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
المقنعة لرجال الدين حينذاك. أما اليوم فإن المفترض أن يكون رجل العلم أكثر معرفة واستنارة، فإنه وإن لم يقتنع بتلك الإجابات الدينية، لكنه لا يستطيع أن يدير ظهره لمباحث حول النشأة والوجود ،والمصير، إذ مثل هذه المباحث قضايا علمية تستحق الاحترام الكامل، لأنها ليست مجردة عن الطبيعة الإنسانية، بل هي عميقة الجذور فيها.
إن الكنيسة إذا أخطأت في إجاباتها فلا يعني ذلك أنَّ الأسئلة ذاتها لا تستحق القبول والتدبّر الكاملين ومن المسلَّم به الآن - يقول ماسلو - أن علماء النفس الطبيعيين والإنسانيين سوف يعتبرون كل شخص لا يهتم بالدين وموضوعاته وقضاياه إنما هو إنسان شاذ ومريض(١).
ثالثا: إن هناك طريقة إجرائية تسهم في عملية التكامل المنشود بين فروع المعرفة، وذلك عن طريق:
أ - طائفة من المتخصصين في علوم (الدنيا) تدرس مبادئ الدين في عقائده ومظاهر العبادة فيه، كما تدرس اللغة لتستطيع أن تقرأ بها وتكتب وتتكلم وتترجم.
طائفة ب
من المتخصصين في علوم (الدين) تأخذ مبادئ من علوم الكون والحياة، ويكون لديهم نصيب من أساسيات الرياضيات والعلوم والجغرافيا والتاريخ البشري العام ولغة أجنبية. ومما يجدر التنويـه بـه عنـد ذكـر هـذه الطائفة أن التأهيل الديني على نحو من العمق والتخصص الحقيقي لن يتأتى في المرحلة الجامعية فقط، ما لم يتشرب المتعلمون علوم الدين في المراحل الثلاث الأولى (٢).
(۱) إبراهام ماسلو، خطر الانشقاق بين الدين والعلم، ۱۷ - ۱۹. (۲) أحمد البيلي، التصور الإسلامي لمناهج التربية والتعليم، نقلاً عن أزمة التعليم الإسلامي لسيد حسين وسيد أشرف، ۸۳).
وكما أمر الرسول - - باتباع ملة إبراهيم، فقد نهى أتباعه من المؤمنين عن التفكير في مخالفة هذا المنهج وزجر الخارجين عن ذلك، وعدّ هذا الخروج - إن حصل - ضربًا من السفاهة : ﴿وَمَنْ يَرْغَبُ عَنْ مِلَّةِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِلَّا مَنْ سَفِهَ نفْسَهُ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٣٠/٢].
ودعا المؤمنين إلى الإيمان بأصول المعارف السماوية وحذرهم في آن واحد من مغبة مخالفة ذلك: ويا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا آمِنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ وَالْكِتَابِ الَّذِي نَزَّلَ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ وَالْكِتابِ الَّذِي أَنْزَلَ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَمَنْ يَكْفُرْ بِاللَّهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ فَقَدْ ضَلَّ ضَلَالاً بَعِيداً [النساء: ١٣٦/٤].
وجاء ذكر من يتسم تفكيره بالفهم التوحيدي لمعارف الوحي في سياق الثناء على المؤمنين: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ ..... [البقرة: ٤/٢].
وهكذا فإن الرسول ومعه المؤمنون يؤمنون بوحدة جميع معارف الوحي على أساس وحدة مصدرها وهو الله تعالى المصدر المطلق
آمَنَ الرَّسُولُ بما أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ رَبِّهِ وَالْمُؤْمِنُونَ كُلٌّ آمَنَ باللهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ لا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ وَقَالُوا سَمِعْنَا وَأَطَعْنَا غُفْرَانَكَ رَبَّنَا
وَإِلَيْكَ الْمَصِيرُ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٥/٢].
وعلى ذلك فإن وحدة المعرفة تتضمن الأصول الكلية للتربية، بما يمثل فلسفة تربوية منفتحة واعية.
Chapter Two: First Section - Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity. Persuasive for the clergymen of that time. Today, it is assumed that the man of science is more knowledgeable and enlightened; even if he is not convinced by those religious answers, he cannot turn his back on inquiries about origin, existence, and destiny, for such inquiries are scientific issues deserving full respect, because they are not abstracted from human nature but are deeply rooted in it. If the church erred in its answers, that does not mean that the questions themselves do not deserve acceptance and full contemplation. It is now taken for granted - says Maslow - that natural and humanistic psychologists will consider every person who does not care about religion and its topics and issues as an abnormal and sick person (1). Third: There is a procedural method that contributes to the desired integration between branches of knowledge, namely: A - A group of specialists in the sciences (of this world) study the principles of religion in its beliefs and manifestations of worship, and also study language to be able to read, write, speak and translate. Group B: Specialists in the sciences (of religion) take principles from the sciences of the universe and life, and have a share of basics in mathematics, sciences, geography, general human history, and a foreign language. It is worth noting when mentioning this group that religious qualification with depth and real specialization cannot be achieved at the university stage only, unless learners absorb religious sciences in the first three stages (2). (1) Abraham Maslow, The Danger of the Split between Religion and Science, 17-19. (2) Ahmed al-Bayli, The Islamic Conception of Curricula of Education, quoted from The Crisis of Islamic Education by Syed Hussain and Syed Ashraf, 83). And just as the Messenger commanded following the religion of Abraham, he forbade his followers from thinking about contradicting this methodology and rebuked those who deviate from it, and considered this deviation - if it occurs - a kind of foolishness: {And who turns away from the religion of Abraham except a fool?} [Al-Baqara 2:130]. And he called the believers to believe in the principles of heavenly knowledge and warned them at the same time of the consequence of contradicting that: {O you who have believed, believe in Allah and His Messenger and the Book that He sent down upon His Messenger and the Scripture which He sent down before. And whoever disbelieves in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Last Day has certainly gone far astray} [An-Nisa 4:136]. And mention came of those whose thinking is characterized by a monotheistic understanding of the knowledge of revelation in the context of praising the believers: {And those who believe in what has been revealed to you, [O Muhammad], and what was revealed before you...} [Al-Baqara 2:4]. Thus, the Messenger and with him the believers believe in the unity of all knowledge of revelation on the basis of the unity of its source, which is Allah Almighty, the absolute source: {The Messenger has believed in what was revealed to him from his Lord, and the believers as well. All have believed in Allah, His angels, His books, and His messengers, [saying], 'We make no distinction between any of His messengers.' And they say, 'We hear and we obey. [We seek] Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the destination'} [Al-Baqara 2:285]. And accordingly, the unity of knowledge includes the universal principles of education, representing an open and conscious educational philosophy.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the ethics and unity of knowledge from a modern Islamic perspective. The author begins by asserting that religious questions about origin, existence, and destiny are deeply rooted in human nature and deserve scientific respect, despite any errors in historical answers by the church. The author then cites Abraham Maslow to argue that disregard for religion is now considered abnormal by psychologists. The author proposes a procedural method for integrating religious and secular sciences: one group of specialists in worldly sciences studies religious principles, while another group of religious specialists acquires basics in secular sciences. This integration, the author argues, is necessary for genuine religious qualification, which cannot be achieved solely at the university level without early grounding. The author then turns to Islamic sources, citing Quranic verses that command following the religion of Abraham, believe in all divine revelations, and emphasize the unity of all revealed knowledge originating from God. The passage concludes that the unity of knowledge comprises universal educational principles and an open, conscious educational philosophy.

Key Terms
وحدة المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the proper attitude towards religious questions and sciences?
A) They are outdated and irrelevant to modern science.
B) They are deep-rooted human concerns that deserve serious consideration, and integration with secular sciences is necessary.
C) They should be rejected because the church made errors.
D) Only religious scholars need to study them.

Key Takeaway
The unity of knowledge in Islam is rooted in tawhid: all true knowledge ultimately derives from Allah, demanding an integrated approach to education that bridges religious and secular sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a verse from the Quran (besides those cited) that emphasizes the unity of revelation and explain how it supports the concept of wahdat al-ma'rifa.
?
Design a brief curriculum for a university course that embodies the two-way integration proposed in the passage: what would a student in Group A learn, and what would a student in Group B learn?

Unity of Revelation through Tawhid
Quranic proof for unity of revelation via tawhid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic evidence for the unity of all revealed knowledge and articulate how it derives from the principle of tawhid.

Core Idea
The unity of revelation is rooted in the oneness of its divine source, Allah.

This passage presents a foundational epistemological claim: that all revealed knowledge forms a unity because it originates from the same divine source. The author supports this by citing Quranic verses that command belief in all scriptures and warn against distinguishing between prophets. Understanding this unity is essential for any Muslim intellectual framework, as it shapes how we approach knowledge across disciplines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
Read the passage and locate where the author explicitly states the unity of revealed knowledge. Look for the phrase 'unity of all knowledge of revelation' and note the basis given.
The claim is found near the end: 'the unity of all knowledge of revelation on the basis of the unity of its source, which is Allah'.
2
Extract the Quranic evidence
The passage cites three verses: Al-Baqarah 2:130, An-Nisa 4:136, and Al-Baqarah 2:4 and 2:285. List what each verse commands or praises regarding belief in previous scriptures.
Verses 4:136 and 2:285 explicitly mention believing in all books and messengers without distinction.
3
Analyze the logical connection
How does tawhid (oneness of Allah) entail the unity of revealed knowledge? The argument is that since all revelation comes from the same source, it must be coherent and unified. Identify this logical step in the passage.
The author connects the unity of source directly to the unity of knowledge in the final sentence.
4
Apply to educational philosophy
The author concludes that this unity of knowledge 'includes the universal principles of education, representing an open and conscious educational philosophy.' Consider how this principle would affect the design of an Islamic curriculum.
Think about how subjects like fiqh, tafsir, and kalam would be integrated rather than isolated.

Source Text

وكما أمر الرسول - ﷺ - باتباع ملة إبراهيم، فقد نهى أتباعه من المؤمنين عن التفكير في مخالفة هذا المنهج وزجر الخارجين عن ذلك، وعدّ هذا الخروج - إن حصل - ضربًا من السفاهة : ﴿وَمَنْ يَرْغَبُ عَنْ مِلَّةِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِلَّا مَنْ سَفِهَ نَفْسَهُ﴾ [البقرة: ١٣٠/٢]. ودعا المؤمنين إلى الإيمان بأصول المعارف السماوية وحذرهم في آن واحد من مغبة مخالفة ذلك: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا آمِنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ وَالْكِتَابِ الَّذِي نَزَّلَ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ وَالْكِتَابِ الَّذِي أَنْزَلَ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَمَنْ يَكْفُرْ بِاللَّهِ وَمَلَائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ فَقَدْ ضَلَّ ضَلَالًا بَعِيدًا﴾ [النساء: ١٣٦/٤]. وجاء ذكر من يتسم تفكيره بالفهم التوحيدي لمعارف الوحي في سياق الثناء على المؤمنين: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكَ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ﴾ [البقرة: ٤/٢]. وهكذا فإن الرسول ومعه المؤمنون يؤمنون بوحدة جميع معارف الوحي على أساس وحدة مصدرها وهو الله تعالى المصدر المطلق: ﴿آمَنَ الرَّسُولُ بِمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ رَبِّهِ وَالْمُؤْمِنُونَ كُلٌّ آمَنَ بِاللَّهِ وَمَلَائِكَتِهِ وَكُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ لَا نُفَرِّقُ بَيْنَ أَحَدٍ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ وَقَالُوا سَمِعْنَا وَأَطَعْنَا غُفْرَانَكَ رَبَّنَا وَإِلَيْكَ الْمَصِيرُ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٥/٢]. وعلى ذلك فإن وحدة المعرفة تتضمن الأصول الكلية للتربية، بما يمثل فلسفة تربوية منفتحة واعية.
And just as the Prophet commanded following the religion of Abraham, he forbade his followers from thinking of opposing this methodology and rebuked those who deviate, and considered this deviation - if it occurs - a kind of foolishness: 'And who would turn away from the religion of Abraham except one who fools himself?' [Al-Baqarah 2:130]. And he called the believers to believe in the principles of heavenly knowledge and warned them simultaneously of the consequence of opposing that: 'O you who have believed, believe in Allah and His Messenger and the Book that He sent down upon His Messenger and the Scripture which He sent down before. And whoever disbelieves in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Last Day has certainly strayed into clear error' [An-Nisa 4:136]. And mention came of those whose thinking is characterized by tawhidi understanding of the knowledge of revelation in the context of praise of the believers: 'And those who believe in what has been revealed to you, and what was revealed before you' [Al-Baqarah 2:4]. Thus the Prophet and with him the believers believe in the unity of all knowledge of revelation on the basis of the unity of its source, which is Allah, the absolute source: 'The Messenger has believed in what was revealed to him from his Lord, and the believers have believed. All have believed in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, [saying], "We make no distinction between any of His messengers." And they say, "We hear and we obey. [We seek] Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the destination"' [Al-Baqarah 2:285]. Therefore the unity of knowledge includes the universal principles of education, representing an open and conscious educational philosophy.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage establishes the Quranic basis for the unity of all revealed knowledge. The author begins by citing the Prophet's command to follow the religion of Abraham and the warning against deviation from this path. Then, verses from the Quran are presented to demonstrate that believers are commanded to believe in all scriptures without distinction. The verse from An-Nisa 4:136 explicitly commands belief in all books, and the verse from Al-Baqarah 2:285 shows that believers affirm the unity of revelation. The author concludes that this unity of knowledge encompasses the universal principles of education, forming a comprehensive educational philosophy rooted in tawhid.

The Quran commands belief in all scriptures because they share a single divine origin, establishing the unity of revealed knowledge as a foundational principle for Islamic thought and education.

Quranic Call to Tawhid as Common Ground with People of the Book
Author explains Quranic call to People of the Book for unity on tawhid and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic strategy of appealing to a common word (kalimat sawa') and demanding proof (burhan) from previous scriptures.

Core Idea
The Quran unites by tawhid, not by denying differences, and demands proof from revelation.

The Quran's approach to the People of the Book is not mere tolerance but a call to the foundational truth of tawhid. This lesson unpacks how the Quran uses the concept of a 'common word' and challenges dissenters to produce proof from their own scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
Read Q. 3:64. The Quran calls to a 'common word' (kalimat sawa'). What is that common word? It is defined as worshipping only Allah, not associating partners, and not taking each other as lords.
The common word is not a vague agreement but a specific theological principle.
2
Analyze the condition
Notice that the common word has three clear conditions: worship of Allah alone, avoidance of shirk, and rejection of human lordship. This shows the Quran does not compromise on tawhid.
These conditions are non-negotiable.
3
Notice the challenge
In Q. 21:24, the Quran challenges the People of the Book to bring a proof (burhan) from their own scriptures if they disagree with tawhid. This places the burden of proof on them.
The proof must come from their own revealed knowledge.
4
Understand the argument
Q. 5:68 states that the People of the Book are 'on nothing' unless they establish the Torah, Gospel, and the Quran. This implies that their own scriptures confirm tawhid, so rejecting it means abandoning their own revelation.
The Quran thus uses internal evidence from their own texts.
5
Draw the educational implication
The author concludes that the call to unity is based on critical examination and scrutiny, not mere reconciliation. Fair-minded People of the Book affirm this cognitive unity.
This is a methodological principle for interfaith dialogue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها. أهل الكتاب ووحدة المعرفة. إن القرآن حين دعا إلى وحدة معارف الوحي قد ارتكز في دعوته تلك على الوحدانية - كما سبقت الإشارة - إذ هي مرتكز جميع دعوات السماء. ومن هنا نجد خطاب القرآن لأهل الكتاب قد استند إلى هذا القاسم المشترك، فدعاهم إلى كلمة سواء هي التوحيد ونبذ الشرك، وتلك حقيقة الإسلام التوحيدي: ﴿قُلْ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ أَلَّا نَعْبُدَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ وَلَا نُشْرِكَ بِهِ شَيْئًا وَلَا يَتَّخِذَ بَعْضُنَا بَعْضًا أَرْبَابًا مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ فَإِنْ تَوَلَّوْا فَقُولُوا اشْهَدُوا بِأَنَّا مُسْلِمُونَ﴾ [آل عمران: ٦٤/٣]. وتحداهم أن يقدموا برهانا يخالف ذلك من خلال معارف الوحي السابقة: ﴿أَمِ اتَّخَذُوا مِنْ دُونِهِ آلِهَةً قُلْ هَاتُوا بُرْهَانَكُمْ هَذَا ذِكْرُ مَنْ مَعِيَ وَذِكْرُ مَنْ قَبْلِي بَلْ أَكْثَرُهُمْ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ الْحَقَّ فَهُمْ مُعْرِضُونَ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٤/٢١]. وحاججهم في ذلك المعنى فقال: ﴿قُلْ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لَسْتُمْ عَلَى شَيْءٍ حَتَّى تُقِيمُوا التَّوْرَاةَ وَالْإِنْجِيلَ وَمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكُمْ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٨/٥]. والمقصود بـ ﴿وَمَا أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكُمْ مِنْ رَبِّكُمْ﴾ القرآن كما قيل في أحد وجهي التفسير. والمتضمن التربوي هنا أن الدعوة إلى تبني الأصول الكلية للتربية مبني على أساس من النقد والتمحيص وليس التوفيق كيفما كان. والمنصفون من أهل الكتاب يؤكدون على حقيقة الوحدة المعرفية بين معارف الوحي جميعها.
The second chapter, first section: Ethics of knowledge and its unity. The People of the Book and the unity of knowledge. Indeed, when the Quran called for the unity of the knowledge of revelation, it based that call on monotheism (tawhid) - as previously indicated - for it is the foundation of all heavenly messages. Hence we find that the Quran's address to the People of the Book relied on this common ground, calling them to a common word: tawhid and rejection of shirk, and that is the reality of tawhidi Islam: 'Say, O People of the Book, come to a common word between us and you: that we worship none but Allah, and that we associate nothing with Him, and that none of us take others as lords besides Allah. But if they turn away, then say, testify that we are Muslims' [Aal-Imran 3:64]. And He challenged them to produce a proof contradicting that from the previous revealed knowledge: 'Or have they taken other than Him as gods? Say, bring your proof. This is the remembrance of those with me and the remembrance of those before me. But most of them do not know the truth, so they are turning away' [Al-Anbiya 21:24]. And He argued with them in that meaning, saying: 'Say, O People of the Book, you are on nothing until you establish the Torah and the Gospel and what was revealed to you from your Lord' [Al-Ma'idah 5:68]. And what is meant by 'what was revealed to you from your Lord' is the Quran, as said in one interpretation. The educational implication here is that the call to adopt the universal principles of education is based on criticism and scrutiny, not mere reconciliation. And the fair-minded among the People of the Book affirm the reality of cognitive unity among all knowledge of revelation.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage focuses on the Quran's approach to the People of the Book (Jews and Christians). The author begins by explaining that the Quran's call to unity of knowledge is rooted in tawhid, which is the foundation of all divine messages. Then, the author cites the famous verse from Aal-Imran 3:64 calling to a common word (kalimat sawa') of tawhid. This is followed by a challenge from Al-Anbiya 21:24 to bring proof (burhan) if they disagree. The argument is strengthened by the verse from Al-Ma'idah 5:68, which states that the People of the Book are on nothing unless they establish the Torah, Gospel, and the Quran. The author notes that 'what was revealed to you' refers to the Quran. Finally, the author draws an educational implication: the call to adopt universal principles of education must be based on critical examination, not mere syncretism. Fair-minded People of the Book themselves affirm this cognitive unity.

برهان

B) A proof from previous revelations

Key Takeaway
The Quran's call to unity is founded on tawhid as a common principle, reinforced by a demand for proof from the People of the Book's own scriptures.

?

Cognitive Unity through Quranic Dialogue
Quranic verses establishing unity through dialogue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Quranic verses promote cognitive unity through commanded best dialogue and shared beliefs.

Core Idea
The Quran commands best dialogue to achieve cognitive unity among believers.

This lesson explores a key Quranic method: using dialogue with the People of the Book to establish common ground. You will see how specific verses lay the foundation for unity of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key verses cited
Find the verses from Surah Al-Qasas and Al-Ankabut in the passage. Notice how they address those who received scripture before the Quran.
The author quotes these verses to illustrate his point.
2
Extract the command and its purpose
What does the Quran command regarding dialogue with the People of the Book? What is the goal? Focus on 'Wa la tujadilu...'.
The purpose is not mere argumentation but achieving cognitive unity.
3
Determine the shared elements
Look at the phrase 'We believe in that which has been revealed to us and revealed to you' and 'our God and your God is one'. What common ground is emphasized?
Shared truth and monotheism are key.
4
Analyze the outcome
How does this approach lead to cognitive unity? What does the author mean by 'al-waḥdah al-maʿrifiyyah'?
Cognitive unity is the recognition of shared truths despite differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها
﴿وَلَقَدْ وَصَّلْنا لَهُمُ الْقَوْلَ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِ هُمْ بِهِ يُؤْمِنُونَ، وَإِذا يُتْلَى عَلَيْهِمْ قَالُوا آمَنَّا بِهِ إِنَّهُ الْحَقُّ مِنْ رَبِّنَا إِنَّا كُنَا مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مُسْلِمِينَ ﴾ [القصص: ٥١/٢٨-٥٣].
وحين نهى القرآن عن الجدال مع أهل الكتاب إلا بأحسن أساليب الحوار شدّد على ضرورة التركيز على حجم الوحدة المعرفية بين الجميع، وهذا ما يعترف به المنصفون من علمائهم:
وَلا تُجادِلُوا أَهْلَ الْكِتابِ إِلا بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا مِنْهُمْ وَقُولُوا آمَنَا بِالَّذِي أُنْزِلَ إِلَيْنَا وَأُنْزِلَ إِلَيْكُمْ وَإِلَهُنا وَإِلَهُكُمْ وَاحِدٌ وَنَحْنُ لَهُ
مُسْلِمُونَ [العنكبوت: ٤٦/٢٩ - ٤٧].
وهاهنا نجد القرآن يقرر أسلوبًا من أساليب التعلم وهو الحوار والمجادلة،
ولكن بأحسن طريق كي تتحقق الوحدة المعرفية على النحو المبتغى.
وتمثل أصول الأخلاق – إلى جانب التوحيد – أساسا آخر يجمع أتباع معارف الوحي كلّهم، ووسيلة من وسائل توحيد مصدر التلقي لتلك المعارف: الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوباً عِنْدَهُمْ فِي التّوْرَاةِ وَالإِنْجِيلِ يَأْمُرُهُمْ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ وَيَنْهَاهُمْ عَنِ الْمُنْكَرِ وَيُحِلُّ لَهُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَيُحَرِّمُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْخَبَائِثَ وَيَضَعُ عَنْهُمْ إِصْرَهُمْ وَالأَغْلالَ الَّتِي كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ فَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِهِ وَعَزَّرُوهُ وَنَصَرُوهُ وَاتَّبَعُوا النُّورَ الَّذِي أُنْزِلَ مَعَهُ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٥٧/٧ ].
وهذا يتضمن أصول التربية الأخلاقية لدى جميع أتباع معارف الوحي. وتقترن بعض مفردات أصول الأخلاق مع بعض أركان الإسلام، كما نجد
ذلك فيما يلي:
عن إسماعيل - عليه السلام - قال تعالى عن الصدق مقرونا بالصلاة والزكاة: وَاذْكُرْ فِي الْكِتابِ إِسْمَاعِيلَ إِنَّهُ كانَ صادِقَ الْوَعْدِ وَكَانَ رَسُولاً نَبيّاً، وَكانَ يَأْمُرُ أَهْلَهُ بالصَّلاةِ وَالزَّكاةِ وَكانَ عِنْدَ رَبِّهِ مَرْضِيّاً [مريم: ٥٤/١٩ -٥٥]. وعن أبناء إبراهيم إسحاق ويعقوب قال سبحانه عن فعل الخير والإحسان مقروناً بالصلاة والزكاة كذلك:
وَوَهَبْنَا لَهُ إِسْحَاق وَيَعْقُوبَ نافِلَةً وَكُلاً جَعَلْنَا صَالِحِينَ، وَجَعَلْنَاهُمْ أَئِمَّةً يَهْدُونَ بِأَمْرِنَا وَأَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْهِمْ فِعْلَ الْخَيْرَاتِ وَإِقَامَ الصَّلَاةِ وَإِيتَاءَ الزَّكَاةِ وَكَانُوا لنا عابدين [الأنبياء: ۷۲/۲۱-۷۳].
واعتماداً على التوحيد والعمل الصالح فإن القرآن يعلن الأمان إلى الأطراف
جميعها:
وإنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا وَالصَّابِئُونَ وَالنَّصَارَى مَنْ آمَنَ بِاللهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ وَعَمِلَ  َصالِحاً فَلا خَوْفٌ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا هُمْ يَحْزَنُونَ﴾ [المائدة: ٦٩/٥. وهذا يدل بالتأكيد على أن العقيدة مكوّن رئيس للسلوك، وأن العلاقة بين العقيدة والسلوك علاقة الكل بالجزء، أو العام بالخاص وذلك ما
tتبناه التربية الإسلامية في إطار موضوع الإيديولوجيا والتربية.
Chapter Two: Chapter One: Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity. 'And indeed We have conveyed to them the word that they might remember. Those to whom We gave the Scripture before it, they believe in it. And when it is recited to them, they say, "We believe in it; indeed, it is the truth from our Lord. Indeed we were, before it, Muslims."' [Al-Qasas 28:51-53]. And when the Quran forbade arguing with the People of the Book except in the best manner of dialogue, it emphasized the necessity of focusing on the extent of cognitive unity among all, and this is what the fair-minded among their scholars acknowledge: 'And do not argue with the People of the Book except in a way that is best, except those who have wronged among them, and say, "We believe in that which has been revealed to us and revealed to you, and our God and your God is one, and we are Muslims to Him."' [Al-Ankabut 29:46-47]. And here we find the Quran establishing a method of learning, which is dialogue and argumentation, but in the best way so that cognitive unity is achieved in the desired manner. And the principles of ethics—alongside tawheed—represent another foundation that gathers all followers of the knowledge of revelation, and a means of unifying the source of reception for that knowledge: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered prophet, whom they find written in what they have of the Torah and the Gospel, who enjoins upon them what is right and forbids them what is wrong and makes lawful for them the good things and prohibits for them the evil and relieves them of their burden and the shackles that were upon them. So they who have believed in him, honored him, supported him, and followed the light that was sent down with him—it is those who will be the successful.' [Al-A'raf 7:157]. And this includes the principles of ethical education for all followers of the knowledge of revelation. And some elements of the principles of ethics are coupled with some pillars of Islam, as we find in the following: Regarding Isma'il—peace be upon him—the Exalted said about truthfulness coupled with prayer and zakat: 'And mention in the Book, Isma'il. Indeed, he was true to his promise, and he was a messenger and a prophet. And he used to enjoin on his people prayer and zakat and was acceptable to his Lord.' [Maryam 19:54-55]. And regarding the sons of Ibrahim, Ishaq and Ya'qub, He said about doing good and excellence coupled with prayer and zakat as well: 'And We gave him Ishaq and Ya'qub as a gift, and each We made righteous. And We made them leaders guiding by Our command, and We inspired to them the doing of good deeds, establishment of prayer, and giving of zakat; and they were worshipers of Us.' [Al-Anbiya 21:72-73]. And relying on tawheed and righteous deed, the Quran declares security for all parties: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews and the Sabeans and the Christians—whoever has believed in God and the Last Day and done righteous deed—no fear will come upon them, nor will they grieve.' [Al-Ma'idah 5:69]. And this certainly indicates that creed is a main component of behavior, and that the relationship between creed and behavior is a relationship of the whole to the part, or the general to the specific, and this is what Islamic education adopts within the framework of the topic of ideology and education.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the Quran's emphasis on the unity of knowledge through ethical dialogue and shared moral principles. The author begins by quoting a verse from Surah Al-Qasas, which shows that those who received previous scripture recognize the truth of the Quran, establishing a cognitive unity. Then, the author cites the Quranic command to argue with the People of the Book only in the best manner, emphasizing that the goal is cognitive unity. This is followed by a verse from Surah Al-A'raf describing the Prophet Muhammad as found in the Torah and Gospel, highlighting ethical commands (enjoining good, forbidding evil, making lawful good things, etc.) as a common foundation. The author then notes that this includes principles of ethical education for all followers of revelation. The passage proceeds to illustrate how ethical principles (like truthfulness) are coupled with pillars of Islam (prayer and zakat) through the examples of Prophet Isma'il and the sons of Prophet Ibrahim. Finally, a verse from Al-Ma'idah is quoted to show that security is granted to all who believe in God and the Last Day and do righteous deeds, indicating that creed is a main component of behavior, and the relationship between creed and behavior is like the whole to the part. The passage concludes by stating that Islamic education adopts this framework within the context of ideology and education.

Common Ethical Foundations for Knowledge Unity
Quranic verses linking ethics and creed for unity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify common ethical principles shared among followers of revelation and explain how they are linked to creed (tawḥīd) in the Quran.

Core Idea
Ethics and tawheed together form the bedrock of Quranic unity.

Building on the previous lesson, this lesson examines how the Quran presents ethical principles alongside tawheed as a universal foundation. You will see examples from prophets that link ethics with pillars of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ethical principles mentioned
Look at Surah Al-A'raf 7:157 and the examples of Isma'il and Ibrahim's sons. What are the key ethical commands? List them: enjoining good, forbidding evil, truthfulness, doing good deeds.
These are universal ethical commands.
2
Notice the coupling with worship
How are ethical actions (truthfulness, doing good) linked to prayer and zakat in the verses? Observe the pattern: the prophets combined ethics with pillars of Islam.
This shows ethics are not separate from worship.
3
Analyze the relationship between creed and behavior
From Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:69, what are the three conditions for security? How does this show that creed is a component of behavior? The passage says creed is the whole, behavior the part.
This indicates a holistic relationship.
4
Synthesize the Quran's method
How does the Quran use these elements to establish unity of knowledge among all followers of revelation? Consider the role of common ethics and shared belief in one God.
This method unifies regardless of particular rituals.

﴿وَلَقَدْ وَصَّلْنا لَهُمُ الْقَوْلَ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِ هُمْ بِهِ يُؤْمِنُونَ، وَإِذا يُتْلَى عَلَيْهِمْ قَالُوا آمَنَّا بِهِ إِنَّهُ الْحَقُّ مِنْ رَبِّنَا إِنَّا كُنَا مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مُسْلِمِينَ ﴾ [القصص: ٥١/٢٨-٥٣].
وحين نهى القرآن عن الجدال مع أهل الكتاب إلا بأحسن أساليب الحوار شدّد على ضرورة التركيز على حجم الوحدة المعرفية بين الجميع، وهذا ما يعترف به المنصفون من علمائهم:

مُسْلِمُونَ [العنكبوت: ٤٦/٢٩ - ٤٧].
وهاهنا نجد القرآن يقرر أسلوبًا من أساليب التعلم وهو الحوار والمجادلة،
ولكن بأحسن طريق كي تتحقق الوحدة المعرفية على النحو المبتغى.
وتمثل أصول الأخلاق – إلى جانب التوحيد – أساسا آخر يجمع أتباع معارف الوحي كلّهم، ووسيلة من وسائل توحيد مصدر التلقي لتلك المعارف: الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوباً عِنْدَهُمْ فِي التّوْرَاةِ وَالإِنْجِيلِ يَأْمُرُهُمْ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ وَيَنْهَاهُمْ عَنِ الْمُنْكَرِ وَيُحِلُّ لَهُمُ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَيُحَرِّمُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْخَبَائِثَ وَيَضَعُ عَنْهُمْ إِصْرَهُمْ وَالأَغْلالَ الَّتِي كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ فَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِهِ وَعَزَّرُوهُ وَنَصَرُوهُ وَاتَّبَعُوا النُّورَ الَّذِي أُنْزِلَ مَعَهُ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٥٧/٧ ].

tتبناه التربية الإسلامية في إطار موضوع الإيديولوجيا والتربية.
Chapter Two: Chapter One: Ethics of Knowledge and Its Unity. 'And indeed We have conveyed to them the word that they might remember. Those to whom We gave the Scripture before it, they believe in it. And when it is recited to them, they say, "We believe in it; indeed, it is the truth from our Lord. Indeed we were, before it, Muslims."' [Al-Qasas 28:51-53]. And when the Quran forbade arguing with the People of the Book except in the best manner of dialogue, it emphasized the necessity of focusing on the extent of cognitive unity among all, and this is what the fair-minded among their scholars acknowledge: 'And do not argue with the People of the Book except in a way that is best, except those who have wronged among them, and say, "We believe in that which has been revealed to us and revealed to you, and our God and your God is one, and we are Muslims to Him."' [Al-Ankabut 29:46-47]. And here we find the Quran establishing a method of learning, which is dialogue and argumentation, but in the best way so that cognitive unity is achieved in the desired manner. And the principles of ethics—alongside tawheed—represent another foundation that gathers all followers of the knowledge of revelation, and a means of unifying the source of reception for that knowledge: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered prophet, whom they find written in what they have of the Torah and the Gospel, who enjoins upon them what is right and forbids them what is wrong and makes lawful for them the good things and prohibits for them the evil and relieves them of their burden and the shackles that were upon them. [Al-Ma'idah 5:69]. And this certainly indicates that creed is a main component of behavior, and that the relationship between creed and behavior is a relationship of the whole to the part, or the general to the specific, and this is what Islamic education adopts within the framework of the topic of ideology and education.

Quran's Tasdiq and Haymana
Author explains Quran's method of affirming and overseeing previous scriptures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Quran's methods of tasdiq and haymana and explain how they function in relation to previous scriptures.

Core Idea
The Quran does not reject the past; it affirms truth and oversees error.

The Quran acknowledges the value of earlier revelations, but it does not accept them uncritically. This lesson unpacks the two key concepts—tasdiq (affirmation) and haymana (oversight)—that define the Quran's distinctive approach to the heritage of previous prophets. Understanding these will sharpen your ability to read Quranic references to earlier scriptures with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Note the Quran's dual relationship with previous scriptures: it affirms their divine origin but also corrects distortions. This is not contradiction but a method.
2
Define tasdiq
Tasdiq is the Quran's confirmation of what is authentic and undistorted in earlier scriptures. Find examples in the Quran where it says 'confirming what is with them' (e.g., Surah Al-Baqarah 2:41).
Tasdiq implies agreement only with the original truth, not with later interpolations.
3
Define haymana
Haymana means the Quran acts as a guardian or overseer over previous scriptures. It evaluates them and preserves the core truth while correcting errors. See Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:48.
Haymana gives the Quran authority to judge what is correct in previous books.
4
Apply to an example
Consider the biblical account of Prophet Ibrahim (AS). The Quran affirms his monotheism (tasdiq) but corrects any narrative that associates shirk with him (haymana).
This shows the method in action: not wholesale rejection, but selective affirmation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن وميراث السابقين
إن القرآن إذ يقر بمعارف السابقين ويدعو إلى إقامة وحدة لمعارف الوحـ
بين أتباع الرسالات السماوية، فإنه ينتهج مسلكا متميزا في التعامل مع ميراث السابقين باعتماده أسلوبي التصديق والهيمنة وذلك بأن يوافق كل معرفة فيها لم يطرأ عليها أي تحريف أو انتحال من غير أن يعني ذلك التصديق أو تلك الهيمنة التوقيع على كل معرفة فيها بقطع النظر عن سلامتها من الخطأ، بل
The Quran and the Heritage of Predecessors. Indeed, when the Quran acknowledges the knowledge of the predecessors and calls for establishing a unity of the knowledge of revelation among the followers of the heavenly messages, it pursues a distinguished approach in dealing with the heritage of the predecessors by adopting the two methods of affirmation (tasdiq) and oversight (haymana), in that it agrees with every knowledge in it that has not been subject to any distortion or fabrication, without that affirmation or that oversight meaning endorsing every knowledge in it regardless of its freedom from error, rather
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage introduces the Quran's distinctive methodology in handling the scriptures that came before it. The author states that the Quran acknowledges the knowledge of earlier prophets and calls for cognitive unity among followers of all revealed religions. However, it does not simply accept everything in those scriptures without scrutiny. Instead, it employs two methods: tasdiq (affirmation of what is true) and haymana (oversight or guardianship). The Quran affirms any knowledge that has not been distorted or fabricated, but it does not thereby endorse everything in those scriptures irrespective of error. The passage cuts off at 'bal' (rather), suggesting a contrast or further clarification that is not provided in the given window.

Key Terms
التصديق
الهيمنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Haymana and tahrif
D) Iqrar and inkar

Key Takeaway
The Quran's method of tasdiq and haymana allows it to affirm the truth in previous scriptures while exercising corrective oversight, a balanced approach essential for understanding inter-textual Quranic references.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Quran as Musaddiq and Muhaymin
Author explains Quran's musaddiq and muhaymin roles with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Quran's roles as musaddiq (confirmer) and muhaymin (guardian/dominator) over previous scriptures, and cite the relevant Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The Quran both confirms true revelation and actively dominates distortion.

This lesson explores the dual epistemological role of the Quran in relation to previous scriptures. The passage introduces two key terms: musaddiq and muhaymin. Understanding these terms is essential for grasping how the Quran evaluates and builds upon earlier revelation while rejecting distortions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key terms
Find the terms musaddiq and muhaymin in the Arabic passage and note their occurrences.
Look for 'مصدقا' and 'مهيمنا' in the text.
2
Extract the meaning from context
From the surrounding commentary and Quranic verses, determine what each term implies about the Quran's relationship with previous books.
Consider the verse from Al-Ma'idah 5:48 and the author's explanation.
3
Differentiate the roles
Explain how musaddiq (confirming) complements muhaymin (guarding/dominating). Note that confirmation is of authentic content, domination is over distortions.
The author states that the Quran uncovers distortion (tahrif) and keeps revelation free from smoke and impurity.
4
Apply to the Quranic verses cited
Analyze the verses from Al-Ma'idah 5:48, Al-Ahqaf 46:12, and As-Saff 61:6 to see how these roles are exemplified.
Observe that the Quran confirms the Torah and Gospel while also correcting polytheistic beliefs introduced into them.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول - أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها

يُعمل فيها منهجه التقديري التمحيصي، كي يتميز السليم فيها من المحرف، في صورة عملية استرجاعية شاملة لذلك الميراث تتضمن نقده وتحليله وتطهيره مما الحق به من إضافات واجتهادات تتنافى مع مضمونه (۱). وذلك ما تشير إليه هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال: وَأَنْزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الْكِتابَ بِالْحَقِّ مُصَدِّقًا لِما بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ مِنَ الْكِتابِ وَمُهَيْمِناً عَلَيْهِ... [المائدة: ٤٨/٥].
وإذا كانت مهمة القرآن القيام بدور التواصل والتكامل فإن مهمة ما سبقه من كتب هو القيام بدور التأسيس وهو دور أصيل وتكاملي في آن واحد. وعن هذا المعنى جاء ذكر القرآن للتوراة:
وَمِنْ قَبْلِهِ كِتابُ مُوسَى إِمَاماً وَرَحْمَةً وَهَذَا كِتابٌ مُصَدِّقٌ لِسَاناً عَرَبِيّاً
لِيُنذِرَ الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا وَبُشْرَى لِلْمُحْسِنِينَ ﴾ [الأحقاف: ١٢/٤٦].
وكذلك الحال مع الإنجيل:
﴿وَإِذْ قالَ عِيسَى ابْنُ مَرْيَمَ يَا بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُمْ مُصَدِّقاً لِما بَيْنَ يَدَيَّ مِنَ التَّوْرَاةِ وَمُبَشِّراً بِرَسُولِ يَأْتِي مِنْ بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ.. ﴾ [الصف: ٦/٦١]. والأمر الجدير بالتنبيه هنا أنه على الرغم من دعوة القرآن لإقامة وحدة بين معارف الوحي، وعلى الرغم كذلك من الأهمية التي تحتلها الوحدة الفكرية بين مجموعة ما، فإن ذلك أكثر ما يكون اشتراكا في خصالهم المنهجية في التفكير، بحيث تربطهم تلك الوحدة الفكرية أيما ارتباط، وبعكسها يكون انفراط عقدها (٢) . ومع ذلك كله فإن القرآن يردّ ويسفه المعتقدات الشركية التي أدخلت في تلك الكتب، ويعدّ ذلك مما طالته يد التحريف ولذلك فإن من مهام أسلوبي التصديق والهيمنة كشف ذلك التحريف ليبقى الوحي معافى من الدخن والدخل. وفي هذا الصدد يقول الله تعالى:
(لَقَدْ كَفَرَ الَّذِينَ قالُوا إِنَّ اللهَ هُوَ الْمَسِيحُ ابْنُ مَرْيَمَ وَقَالَ الْمَسِيحُ يَا بَنِي إسرائيلَ اعْبُدُوا اللهَ رَبِّي وَرَبَّكُمْ إِنَّهُ مَنْ يُشْرِكْ بِاللَّهِ فَقَدْ حَرَّمَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الْجَنَّةَ وَمَأْواهُ النَّارُ وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنْصارِ، لَقَدْ كَفَرَ الَّذِينَ قَالُوا إِنَّ اللَّهَ ثَالِثُ ثَلَاثَةٍ وَمَا مِنْ إِلَهِ إِلَّا إِلَهُ واحِدٌ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْتَهُوا عَمَا يَقُولُونَ لَيَمَسَّنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا
مِنْهُمْ عَذابٌ أَلِيمٌ ﴾ [المائدة: ٧٢/٥-٧٣].
وثمة ملاحظات ثلاث في ضوء ما سبق:
الملحوظة الأولى: إقرار مبدأ التراكم المعرفي، وأن يبني اللاحق معارفه من حيث انتهى السابق.
الملحوظة :الثانية: إن أسلوب القرآن في الهيمنة والتصديق على جميع ما سبقه من معارف مصدرها الأصلي هو الوحي يضفي صفة العالمية على فلسفة التربية الإسلامية المنبثقة عن القرآن الكريم ذاته بل ويدفعها لاستخدام الأسلوبين كليهما في وجه الأفكار التربوية الرامية إلى فرض سيطرتها على ما عداها من المذاهب والأفكار الأخرى بما في ذلك فلسفة التربية الإسلامية بطبيعة الحال. وقد يمتد ذلك ليشمل الحكم على الجيد والرديء من نتاج الحضارة الغربية المعاصرة، وفق المنهج عينه.
الملحوظة :الثالثة: إن انطلاق القرآن الكريم من منهجية الهيمنة والتصديق إنما تمّ في ضوء أصول ثابتة هي نصوص القرآن الكريم نفسها، وهي بمثابة أصول يقينية راسخة لم تطلها يد التحريف التي طالت ما سبقها من نصوص الكتب المقدّسة، كما أنها تمثل معياراً منضبطا، ومرجعية حاكمة على المعارف الأخرى.
Chapter Two: Section One - Ethics of Knowledge and its Unity

Its method of estimation and scrutiny is applied, so that the sound is distinguished from the distorted, in the form of a comprehensive retrospective process of that heritage, including its critique, analysis, and purification of what has been attached to it of additions and interpretations that contradict its content (1). That is indicated by this verse - for example: 'And We have sent down to you the Book in truth, confirming what was before it of the Scripture and as a guardian over it...' [Al-Ma'idah 5:48].
And if the mission of the Quran is to play the role of communication and integration, then the mission of the books before it is to play the foundational role, which is an original and integrative role simultaneously. In this sense comes the mention of the Torah in the Quran: 'And before it was the Book of Moses as a guide and a mercy. And this is a confirming Book in an Arabic tongue to warn those who do wrong and as good tidings to the doers of good' [Al-Ahqaf 46:12].
And likewise with the Gospel: 'And when Jesus, son of Mary, said: O Children of Israel, I am the messenger of Allah to you, confirming what came before me of the Torah, and bringing good tidings of a messenger to come after me, whose name is Ahmad...' [As-Saff 61:6]. The point worth noting here is that despite the Quran's call to establish unity among the knowledges of revelation, and despite the importance of intellectual unity among a group, that is most achieved by sharing in their methodological characteristics of thinking, such that this intellectual unity binds them strongly, and its opposite would be the disintegration of its bond (2). Yet despite all that, the Quran rejects and exposes the polytheistic beliefs that have been introduced into those books, and considers that among what the hand of distortion has touched. Therefore, among the tasks of the two methods of confirmation and domination is the uncovering of that distortion so that revelation remains free of smoke and impurity. In this context, Allah Almighty says: 'They have certainly disbelieved who say that Allah is the Messiah, son of Mary, while the Messiah said: O Children of Israel, worship Allah, my Lord and your Lord. Indeed, whoever associates others with Allah - Allah has forbidden him Paradise, and his refuge is the Fire. And there are no helpers for the wrongdoers. They have certainly disbelieved who say that Allah is the third of three. And there is no god except one God. And if they do not desist from what they are saying, there will surely afflict the disbelievers among them a painful punishment' [Al-Ma'idah 5:72-73].
And there are three observations in light of the above:
The first observation: Affirmation of the principle of cumulative knowledge, and that the later person builds his knowledge from where the predecessor left off.
The second observation: That the Quran's method of domination and confirmation over all preceding knowledges whose original source is revelation gives the attribute of universality to the philosophy of Islamic education emanating from the Noble Quran itself, and even pushes it to use both methods in the face of educational ideas aiming to impose their control over other doctrines and ideas, including the philosophy of Islamic education naturally. This may extend to include judging the good and bad of the products of contemporary Western civilization, according to the same methodology.
The third observation: That the launching of the Noble Quran from the methodology of domination and confirmation took place in light of fixed principles, which are the texts of the Noble Quran itself, and they are as firm certain principles that have not been touched by the hand of distortion that touched the previous texts of the sacred books, and they represent a precise standard and a governing reference for other knowledges.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemological role of the Quran in relation to previous scriptures, emphasizing that the Quran serves both as a confirmer (musaddiq) and a guardian (muhaymin). The author begins by stating that the Quran applies a method of estimation and scrutiny to distinguish sound knowledge from distortion in the heritage of revelation, as illustrated by the verse from Surah Al-Ma'idah (5:48). The author then explains the complementary roles: earlier scriptures established foundational knowledge, while the Quran integrates and builds upon them, confirming the truth and rejecting alterations. This is supported by verses about the Torah and Gospel. The author notes that despite the Quran's call for unity among revealed knowledges, this unity is based on shared methodological characteristics; otherwise, its bond would disintegrate. The Quran also rejects polytheistic beliefs that were introduced into those books, and part of its task of confirmation and domination is to uncover that distortion. The passage then presents three observations: first, the principle of cumulative knowledge—that later knowledge builds on earlier; second, the Quran's method of domination and confirmation gives universality to Islamic education and enables it to judge other ideas; third, the Quran's methodology is based on its own fixed, certain texts that serve as a precise standard and governing reference for all other knowledges.

Key Terms
مهيمنا
مصدقا
تحريف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the term muhaymin signify according to the passage?
A) A passive witness that only observes previous scriptures.
B) An active guardian that corrects distortions and dominates over previous scriptures.
C) The source of all knowledge without any reference to earlier books.
D) A negation of all previous scriptures as false.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's roles as musaddiq and muhaymin together ensure that the true content of earlier revelation is preserved while corruptions are rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the Quranic verse Al-Ma'idah 5:48. Explain in one sentence how the verse simultaneously shows confirmation (musaddiq) and domination (muhaymin) over previous scripture.

Three Epistemological Principles from the Quran's Relationship with Previous Scriptures
Author lists three observations about knowledge accumulation and criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the three observations the author draws from the Quran's role, and apply them to evaluate the relationship between Islamic knowledge and other traditions.

Core Idea
The Quran establishes cumulative knowledge, universal authority, and fixed criteria for evaluating all knowledge.

After explaining the Quran's dual role, the author provides three observations that summarize the epistemological implications. These observations form a practical methodology for how Islamic education should interact with prior and contemporary knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the three observations
Locate the three numbered observations in the Arabic passage, which appear after the Quranic verses.
They begin with 'الملحوظة الأولى', 'الملحوظة الثانية', 'الملحوظة الثالثة'.
2
Restate each observation in your own words
Paraphrase the first (cumulative knowledge), second (universality and dominance over other ideas), and third (fixed Quranic principles as criteria).
Ensure you capture the essence: later builds on earlier; Quran's method gives universality to Islamic education; Quran's own texts are the ultimate standard.
3
Connect each observation to the Quran's role as musaddiq and muhaymin
Explain how these observations follow from the dual role of confirmation and domination.
For example, cumulative knowledge relates to confirming what is true from earlier scriptures.
4
Apply the third observation to a real scenario
Consider how the Quran's fixed principles serve as a governing reference for evaluating other knowledges, such as contemporary educational philosophies.
The author explicitly mentions using this methodology to judge products of Western civilization.

الباب الثاني: الفصل الأول - أخلاق المعرفة ووحدتها

يُعمل فيها منهجه التقديري التمحيصي، كي يتميز السليم فيها من المحرف، في صورة عملية استرجاعية شاملة لذلك الميراث تتضمن نقده وتحليله وتطهيره مما الحق به من إضافات واجتهادات تتنافى مع مضمونه (۱). وذلك ما تشير إليه هذه الآية - على سبيل المثال: وَأَنْزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الْكِتابَ بِالْحَقِّ مُصَدِّقًا لِما بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ مِنَ الْكِتابِ وَمُهَيْمِناً عَلَيْهِ... [المائدة: ٤٨/٥].
وإذا كانت مهمة القرآن القيام بدور التواصل والتكامل فإن مهمة ما سبقه من كتب هو القيام بدور التأسيس وهو دور أصيل وتكاملي في آن واحد. وعن هذا المعنى جاء ذكر القرآن للتوراة:

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first observation about the Quran's relationship with previous knowledges?
A) The Quran rejects all previous scriptures as false.
B) The Quran affirms the principle of cumulative knowledge—later builds on earlier.
C) The Quran imposes its methodology without reference to previous books.
D) The Quran only confirms but does not dominate previous knowledges.

The Epistemological Integration of Unseen and Witnessed
Author discusses the relationship between the unseen and witnessed realms and their epistemological integration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Quran integrates the unseen (ghayb) and witnessed (shahada) realms and identify the role of divine laws (sunan) in this integration.

Core Idea
The unseen and witnessed are not separate; the witnessed reveals the unseen's laws, transforming faith into action.

In this passage, the author argues that the Quran presents two interconnected fields of knowledge: the unseen and the witnessed. While the unseen provides spiritual foundation, it can feel passive. The witnessed realm, through the horizons and the selves, activates faith. Understanding the divine laws (sunan) that govern both realms is key to achieving a balanced Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary fields
Locate where the passage explicitly names 'al-ghayb' and 'al-shahada' as the two fields of knowledge. Note that mentioning one necessitates the other in the Muslim mind guided by revelation.
2
Distinguish their characteristics
The unseen gives spiritual strength but can feel passive and private. The witnessed provides another kind of strength through its subsidiary fields: the horizons and the selves, making faith positive and practical.
The author contrasts the emotional experience of the unseen with the active engagement of the witnessed.
3
Identify the subsidiary fields of the witnessed
The passage states that the witnessed realm manifests in 'the horizons (afaq)' and 'the selves (anfus)'. These are the external universe and human introspection.
These two fields are commanded to be reflected upon in the Quran.
4
Explain the relationship between witnessed and unseen
The witnessed realm is not separate; it derives its laws (sunan) from the unseen. Observing the witnessed through faith in the unseen leads to balance and Quranic understanding.
The author uses the example of angelic support being subject to the law of causes to illustrate this.
5
Understand the concept of sunan
The laws (sunan) that govern the horizons and selves originate in the unseen. The goal is to understand these laws as derived from the unseen, linking the two realms.
The passage emphasizes that a proper curriculum must allocate content to these laws while connecting them to their original field, the unseen.

Source Text

العلاقة بين الغيب والشهادة
إن ذكر أحد ميداني المعرفة يستلزم حضوراً للآخر في الذهن بالنسبة إلى المسلم المستهدي بالوحي في تعامله مع نظرية المعرفة بكل مفرداتها. ومما يؤكد هذا المعنى ويجسد أبعاده أنه على الرغم من الأهمية التي يحتلها ميدان الغيب والمزايا التي تجعل المرء يحس بأنه يعيش في كنف الرحمن، ويتذوق حلاوة الإيمان في قلبه إلا أنه يصاحب بشعور من الحرمان الخفي والسلبية في كونها تجربة وجدانية فردية.
ولذلك فإنه إذا كان الإيمان بالغيب يعطي قوة التماسك، فإن آيات عالم الشهادة تزوّد الإنسان بنوع آخر من قوة التماسك المتجلية في ميدانين فرعيين هما الآفاق والأنفس، فيتحول الإيمان إلى صيغة إيجابية عملية، فيتغير الواقع وتتم السيطرة على آيات الله في الآفاق والأنفس. ذلك أن مرحلة الإيمان بعالم الشهادة تمثل مرحلة وعي لفهم ما أمر الله به، وأن ذلك مقتضى العقل والفطرة وعين الصواب. وحين يحدث ذلك الوعي فإن التوازن يتحقق للإنسان على مختلف المستويات، ويتحقق - من ثمّ - منهج القرآن في أمره الناس بالنظر في سير الأمم، والأحداث في الأرض، كيما يروا عالم الشهادة من خلال إيمانهم بحقيقة ما جاء في عالم الغيب.
ثم إنه يلاحظ أن القوانين التي تحكم عالم الشهادة في ميداني الآفاق والأنفس - وهي القوانين التي يسميها القرآن (سنن) - قائمة هي الأخرى في عالم الغيب مما يجعل العقل المتبصر يدرك أن آيات الله التي ظاهرها علم الغيب كإنزال الملائكة للتأييد والنصر يخضع لقانون الأسباب أو السنن الواضحة ذلك أن اتخاذ الرب إلها والاستقامة منهجاً من وراء قانون الأسباب أو السنن. وهنا فإن هدف المنهج يتمثل في إيجاد المتعلم المستوعب لقوانين الشهادة المستمدة من عالم الغيب ليتحقق الارتباط الإيجابي بين الغيب والشهادة. ولن يتم ذلك إلا بتخصيص قدر مناسب من مفردات المحتوى لتناول تلك القوانين، مع الربط بينها وبين عالم الغيب (ميدانها الأصلي).
The relationship between the unseen and the witnessed. Indeed, the mention of one field of knowledge necessitates the presence of the other in the mind for the Muslim guided by revelation in his dealing with the theory of knowledge in all its components. And what confirms this meaning and embodies its dimensions is that despite the importance occupied by the field of the unseen and the merits that make one feel that he lives in the shelter of the Most Merciful and tastes the sweetness of faith in his heart, it is accompanied by a feeling of hidden deprivation and passivity as it is an individual emotional experience. Therefore, if faith in the unseen gives strength of cohesion, then the signs (ayat) of the world of the witnessed provide man with another kind of strength of cohesion manifested in two subsidiary fields: the horizons (afaq) and the selves (anfus), so faith transforms into a positive practical form, reality changes, and control over the signs of Allah in the horizons and the selves is achieved. That is because the stage of faith in the world of the witnessed represents a stage of awareness to understand what Allah commanded, and that is required by reason, innate disposition (fitrah), and is the very truth. When that awareness occurs, balance is achieved for man at various levels, and then the Quranic method is realized in its command to people to reflect on the histories of nations and events on earth, so that they may see the world of the witnessed through their faith in the truth of what came in the world of the unseen. Then it is observed that the laws that govern the world of the witnessed in the fields of the horizons and the selves – which are the laws that the Quran calls 'sunan' (divine laws) – are also established in the world of the unseen, making the discerning mind realize that the signs of Allah whose outward appearance is the science of the unseen, such as the sending down of angels for support and victory, are subject to the law of causes or the clear laws (sunan). That is because taking the Lord as a god and righteousness as a path stems from the law of causes or the sunan. Here the goal of the method is to produce a learner who comprehends the laws of the witnessed derived from the world of the unseen, so that a positive connection between the unseen and the witnessed is achieved. And that will only be achieved by allocating an appropriate amount of content components to address those laws, while linking them to the world of the unseen (their original field).
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the relationship between the two fundamental fields of knowledge in the Quran: the unseen (ghayb) and the witnessed (shahada). The author begins by stating that mentioning one field automatically implies the other in the mind of a Muslim guided by revelation. He then highlights a paradox: although faith in the unseen provides inner strength and a sense of divine shelter, it can also feel like a private, passive experience. To overcome this, the witnessed realm offers another type of strength through two sub-fields: the horizons (the external universe) and the selves (human introspection). Faith thus becomes active and transformative. The author emphasizes that engaging with the witnessed world is an act of consciousness in obedience to Allah, required by reason and innate nature. When this awareness is attained, balance is achieved, and the Quranic method of observing historical events and natural phenomena becomes a means to see the witnessed through the lens of the unseen. The author further notes that the laws (sunan) governing the witnessed world originate from the unseen realm, so even miraculous events like angelic support are subject to these laws. The ultimate educational goal is to produce learners who understand the laws of the witnessed as derived from the unseen, thereby forging a positive link between the two fields. This requires a curriculum that integrates the study of these laws with their unseen foundation.

The Integral Relationship of Ghayb and Shahada in Islamic Education
Author defines the relationship between unseen and witnessed realms and its educational implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the organic, integrative relationship between ghayb and shahada in Islamic education and list the four points that renew the link between religious and empirical sciences.

Core Idea
The unseen and witnessed realms are complementary, not conflicting.

How does Islamic education reconcile the unseen (ghayb) with the observed world (shahada)? This passage from a foundational text on Islamic education argues that the two are not separate domains but form an organic whole. Understanding this relationship is key to seeing how religious and empirical sciences work together toward human purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main framework
Read the first two sentences. The author states that the concept of ghayb and shahada is the most comprehensive framework defining the human intellect, its role, and its limits. This sets the stage for everything else.
This is an epistemological claim: the unseen-witnessed distinction is foundational.
2
Extract the organic relationship
The passage says Islamic education considers the relationship between these two fields as an 'organic, integrative relationship' – not separate or opposed. Note the word 'organic' means they are interdependent.
Organic implies a living connection, not a mechanical one.
3
Analyze the four points
The author lists four specific ways this relationship renews the link between religious and empirical sciences. For each point: (1) knowledge linked to action, goal is worship; (2) cognitive distinction between worship and worldly matters; (3) vicegerency requires both unseen and religious sciences; (4) religion and knowledge are both necessary for human existential purpose.
These are not merely theoretical; they have practical educational implications.
4
Synthesize the educational implication
Combine the four points to understand how they prevent any contradiction between faith and science. The ultimate goal is achieving human purpose: worship (ubudiyya) through vicegerency (khilafah).
This synthesis is the key takeaway for Islamic education.

Chapter Two: Section Two - Field of Knowledge – The Unseen and the Witnessed. The concept of the unseen and the witnessed is the most comprehensive framework that defines the meaning of the human intellect and its role in human life and the limits of this role and its fields. The educational implication specific to the field of the unseen and the witnessed is embodied in the foundation of the philosophy of Islamic education on considering the relationship between the two fields of knowledge (the unseen and the witnessed) as an organic, integrative relationship. Rather, the matter extends in a further educational direction to renew the relationship between religious sciences and empirical sciences through the following: 1. Linking knowledge with action, such that knowledge becomes a means and action a goal, and then knowledge of religion or human sciences achieves a supreme final goal, which is the worship of man to God Almighty. 2. The cognitive – not existential – distinction between matters of worship and matters of sovereignty and empirical vicegerency. In more precise terms, the objective distinction between the worlds of the unseen and the witnessed. 3. The goal of vicegerency for man as a truth of existence and its connection to the knowledge of names has led to the lifting of conflict between belief in unseen matters and religious (human) sciences from the perspective that achieving the goal of vicegerency is not realized except through sciences of the unseen and sciences of religion. 4. There is a correlation between the truth of vicegerency to achieve worship and knowledge to achieve sovereignty, that religion and knowledge are two necessary components for achieving the existential goal of man, which means preventing any contradiction between them.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage sets the epistemological framework for the relationship between the unseen (ghayb) and the witnessed (shahada) realms. The author begins by asserting that the concept of ghayb and shahada is the most comprehensive framework defining the human intellect, its role, and its limits. The educational implication is that Islamic education philosophy is founded on an organic, integrative relationship between these two fields of knowledge. The author then extends this to renew the relationship between religious sciences and empirical sciences through four points. The first point emphasizes linking knowledge to action, making knowledge a means toward the ultimate goal of worship. The second distinguishes cognitively (not existentially) between matters of worship and matters of worldly vicegerency, highlighting objective distinction. The third argues that the goal of vicegerency (khilafah) and its connection to the knowledge of names (from the Quranic story of Adam) removes any conflict between belief in the unseen and religious sciences, since vicegerency requires both. The fourth asserts a mutual necessity: vicegerency leads to worship, knowledge leads to sovereignty, and religion and knowledge are both essential for man's existential purpose, preventing any contradiction.

Key Takeaway
Islamic education views ghayb and shahada as organically integrated fields whose relationship is renewed through linking knowledge to action, a cognitive distinction between worship and vicegerency, the necessity of both for khilafah, and the mutual dependence of religion and science for human purpose.
