Quranic Narratives as Unseen News: Epistemological Foundations
Identifies Quranic stories as unseen news

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the epistemic status of Quranic stories as news of the unseen (anbā' al-ghayb) and distinguish them from ordinary historical reports.

Core Idea
Quranic stories are certain, divinely revealed news of the unseen, not conjectural histories.

This passage from the Nazariyya al-Quran curriculum establishes that the stories of past prophets in the Quran are not ordinary history but belong to the realm of the unseen (ghayb). The verses from Surah Hud and Surah Yusuf explicitly label them as 'anbā' al-ghayb' (news of the unseen) revealed to the Prophet. Understanding this epistemological foundation is crucial for how we approach Quranic narratives as sources of certain knowledge in Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term
Locate the term 'anbā' al-ghayb' in the Arabic passage. Notice it appears in the two Quranic verses cited (Hud 11:49 and Yusuf 12:102). This term is central to the epistemic claim.
In mantiq, khabar is a type of proposition; here it refers specifically to divinely revealed narratives.
2
Examine the proof texts
Read the two verses carefully. In both, the phrase 'tilka/dhalika min anbā' al-ghayb nūḥīhā ilayka' directly states that these stories are unseen news revealed by Allah. The verses also assert that neither the Prophet nor his people knew these details before revelation.
The phrases 'mā kunta taʿlamuhā' and 'wamā kunta ladayhim' emphasise the inaccessibility of this knowledge through ordinary means.
3
Contrast with ordinary history
Ordinary historical reports depend on human transmission and may be uncertain. The Quranic stories, however, are not derived from human sources; they are directly revealed. This elevates their epistemic status from probable (ẓannī) to certain (yaqīnī) knowledge.
The passage explicitly says these stories are at the highest levels of authenticity (aʿlā marātib al-ṣiḥḥa).
4
Understand the epistemological claim
The author claims that Quranic stories are certain in both transmission (riwāya) and understanding (dirāya). Because Allah is the source, there is no possibility of error or distortion. This is the basis for their authority in Islamic education.
This distinguishes Quranic narratives from other historical accounts that may contain inaccuracies.
5
Apply to curriculum methodology
The passage concludes that the curriculum should adopt these stories as the highest truth. This means storytelling in Islamic education is not merely illustrative but carries epistemic weight. Teachers must present them as certain knowledge, not as myths or parables.
Consider how this affects the way you would teach a story like that of the People of the Cave (Surah al-Kahf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And among that which falls within the framework of the unseen world in the Quran are the certain news of the predecessors, as indicated in this verse about Noah, peace be upon him: These are from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you [O Muhammad]; you did not know them, nor did your people before this, so be patient; indeed, the [best] outcome is for the righteous [Hud 11:49]. The curriculum is concerned with adopting the news of the Quran and its stories, and placing them at the highest levels of authenticity in transmission and understanding, and methodologies are concerned with their role in making the story-telling method one of the methods considered when presenting it in the curriculum.

Commentary
This passage classifies Quranic narratives as unseen news (akhbar ghaybiyya). It cites two verses: from Surah Hud about Noah, and from Surah Yusuf about Joseph, both explicitly called 'news of the unseen' (anba' al-ghayb). The author then states that the educational curriculum should rely on these stories as the highest level of authenticity, both in narration (riwaya) and understanding (diraya). The methodology of storytelling is thus affirmed as a valid pedagogical tool within Islamic education.

The Interdependence of Sense and Intellect in Epistemology of the Unseen
Author explains the roles of sense and intellect in acquiring knowledge of the unseen, emphasizing their interdependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why both sense and intellect are necessary (with the exception of primary rational axioms) for acquiring knowledge of the unseen according to this epistemological framework.

Core Idea
Sense and intellect are like two wings: neither can fly alone in the realm of the unseen.

This passage tackles a key epistemological question: if the unseen is by definition beyond sensory perception, how can we know it? The author clarifies that both sensory and rational tools are indispensable, working together, except for the foundational rational laws that are innate. Understanding this interdependent framework is crucial for grasping how Islamic theology grounds its knowledge in both empirical and rational sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two tools
The passage explicitly names al-hass (sense) and al-'aql (intellect) as the primary tools. Note that they are paired together as interdependent.
These are not exhaustive; revelation is also mentioned later.
2
Recognize the exception
The author makes an exception for primary rational laws (qawanin al-'aql al-awwaliyya), which are innate and not derived from sensory experience. They are few and foundational, like the principle of non-contradiction.
These laws are detailed later in the study.
3
Understand the process
The method for knowing the unseen starts from sensory perceptions, then transcends the material framework, interacting with rational principles to grasp major theological truths. This shows sequential synergy.
The process is not purely empirical nor purely rational; it is both.
4
Apply the principle
Consider a specific unseen truth (e.g., the existence of Allah). Sense provides observations of the cosmos; intellect uses these to infer a necessary creator, but detailed knowledge of His attributes comes from revelation.
The interplay ensures comprehensiveness.

Tools for knowing the unseen. If the meaning of the unseen is everything that is definitively absent from the senses, does that mean that the sensory and rational tools of knowledge have no place in the field of the unseen? The answer requires a degree of detail. Here it is advisable to emphasize that it is impossible for either sense or intellect to obtain any knowledge except through both of them together - unless we except the primary rational laws, which will be detailed in the appropriate place in this study - and thus we understand how the relationship between the world of the unseen and the world of the witnessed indicates the possibility of using the two tools of sense and intellect together. For the method of knowledge in the world of the unseen starts from sensory perceptions, transcending the limited material framework, to interact with the primary principles of the intellect, thus enabling the perception of the major issues of the unseen: divinity, lordship, names, attributes, and prophethood, in a manner of scientific knowledge based on the texts of revelation. Likewise, the intellect, through rational reflection, can know some creedal universals such as the existence of Allah Almighty – from the principle of acceptance – and the knowledge of prophethood as a path to unseen knowledge. But neither sense nor intellect can attain knowledge of

Commentary
This passage addresses the epistemological tools for knowing the unseen. The author poses a rhetorical question: if ghayb is what is definitively absent from the senses, does that mean sensory and rational tools are useless in this domain? The answer requires detail. The author emphasizes that sense and intellect work together; neither can obtain knowledge alone, with the exception of primary rational axioms (like the law of non-contradiction). The relationship between the unseen and the witnessed worlds allows both tools to be used. Specifically, the method for knowing the unseen begins with sensory perceptions (e.g., empirical observations) that then interact with the intellect's primary principles, leading to knowledge of major theological truths (e.g., divinity, prophethood), all grounded in revelation. The intellect alone can also grasp some creedal universals, such as the existence of God (in terms of first acceptance) and the concept of prophethood. However, neither sense nor intellect can reach complete knowledge on their own; revelation is necessary. The passage ends abruptly, but the argument is clear.

Key Terms
الحس (al-hass): Sensory perception; the faculty of perceiving material phenomena.
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect; the rational faculty that includes primary principles (qawanin 'aqliyya awwaliyya) and the ability to reason. [Note: In Islamic epistemology, 'aql often includes innate principles; here it is distinguished from sensory tools.]
قوانين العقل الأولية (qawanin al-'aql al-awwaliyya): Primary rational laws, such as the principle of non-contradiction, which are innate and not derived from sensory experience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the exception to the rule that sense and intellect must work together to obtain knowledge?
A) Sensory perception of the unseen
B) The primary rational laws (قوانين العقل الأولية)
C) Revelation alone
D) The imagination

Key Takeaway
In Islamic epistemology, sense and intellect are interdependent tools for knowing the unseen, with only primary rational axioms directly accessible to the intellect independent of sensory experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Revelation as the Unique Source of Knowledge of the Unseen
Author argues for revelation as the unique source of knowledge of the unseen, refuting secular critiques.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the epistemological argument that revelation is the only source of certain knowledge about the unseen, and refute the secular critique that Islamic education creates contradictory logics.

Core Idea
Revelation is the only source for certain knowledge of the unseen, as senses and intellect cannot access it.

In this passage, the author defends the unique epistemic role of revelation in matters beyond sensory perception. He builds on the limitations of the senses and intellect to argue that only certain report (khabar yaqini), i.e., divine revelation, can provide knowledge of the unseen. He then addresses and refutes a secular objection that Islamic education creates conflicting logics. This lesson will walk you through the logical structure of his argument and his critical response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage to determine the thesis. What is the author trying to prove about knowledge of the unseen?
The thesis is that revelation is the only source for certain knowledge of the unseen.
2
Trace the premises
Look at the reasons given: why is revelation needed? Identify the limitations of senses and intellect, and the Quranic evidence cited.
The author mentions sensory deception, the inability to perceive angels, and the creation of heavens being beyond sensory knowledge.
3
Identify the objection
Find the secular critique that the author refutes. What does the objector claim about Islamic education?
The objector claims Islamic education creates two contradictory logics: scientific and unseen-based.
4
Analyze the refutation
How does the author counter the objection? What logical flaw does he point out?
The author argues that the objector himself relies on non-sensory knowledge (history, predictions) and that the dichotomy is false.
5
Evaluate the overall argument
Assess whether the author's argument is sound. Is his reasoning valid? Why or why not?
The argument is valid if one accepts the premise that senses cannot access the unseen and that revelation is the only alternative.

وإذا كان ذلك شأن العقل مع الغيب، فإنه بالنسبة إلى الحس أشد تأكيداً، حيث إن ضعفه عن إدراك تلك المسائل التفصيلية من الغيب يتجلى فيما يعرف بخداع الحواس الذي سيرد تفصيله في المقام المناسب من هذه الدراسة بإذن الله تعالى-. ولكن هذا لا ينصدم بحقائق العلم وضوابطه. فثمة تقرير لدى العلماء مؤداه أن ليس كل مالا تراه العين أو يلمسه الحسّ محكوماً عليه بالانعدام. ولم يسبق لأي من العلماء أن زعم أن سبيل العلم محصورة في أي من الحواس، حيث إن لدى العلماء تقسيمات للمعرفة يجعل جزءاً منها حسياً، وجزءاً غير حسي. ولولا ذلك لما كان ثمة معنى للدراسات التاريخية والتنبؤات المستقبلية(١). وهـو ما يشير من ناحية أخرى إلى عملية تنظيم المعرفة وترتيبها منطقياً. وبالنسبة إلى القرآن الكريم فإن كمّاً هائلاً من المخلوقات غير المحسوسة يسجلها القرآن كالملائكة التي تدخلت لنصر المسلمين الثابتين في معركة حنين: ويا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَةَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذْ جَاءَتْكُمْ جُنُودٌ فَأَرْسَلْنا عَلَيْهِمْ رِيحاً وَجُنُودًا لَمْ تَرَوْهَا وَكانَ اللهُ بِما تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيراً) [الأحزاب: ٩/٣٣]. كما أن معرفة الكيفية التي ابتدأ بها خلق ميداني الأفاق والأنفس مما لا يدخل في نطاق المعرفة الحسية: ﴿وما أَشْهَدْتُهُمْ خَلْقَ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَلَا خَلْقَ أَنْفُسِهِمْ ﴾ [الكهف: ٥١/١٨]. وهؤلاء أبناء يعقوب عليه السلام- يعلنون عجزهم عن حفظ الغيب لأنه من اختصاص الله وحده، وأنى لهم أن يطلعوا بحواسهم على ذلك: ط﴿وَما شَهِدْنَا إِلَّا بِما عَلِمْنَا وَمَا كُنَا لِلْغَيْبِ حَافِظِينَ﴾ [يوسف: ۸۱/۱۲]. وإذا تقرر ذلك تقرر تبعاً له أن مصدر المعرفة الوحيد في قضايا الغيب إنما هو الخبر اليقيني متمثلاً في الوحي، وهو ما ينعكس تلقائياً على التربية الإسلامية في جانبها المعرفي إذ ترتكز على الوحي المعصوم مصدراً وطريقة لها، في التعامل مع ميدان الغيب: ﴿قُلْ إِنَّما أُنْذِرُكُمْ بِالْوَحْي﴾ [الأنبياء: ٤٥/٢١]، وما كُنتَ تَدْرِي مَا الْكِتَابُ وَلا الإيمان وَلَكِنْ جَعَلْنَاهُ نُورًا نَهْدِي بِهِ مَنْ يَشَاءُ مِنْ عبادِنا [الشورى: ٥٢/٤٢]. ولا معنى يبقى بعد ذلك المعترض يرى أن في اعتماد التربية الإسلامية على الوحي ما يزرع في عقول الناشئة منطقين متعارضين: منطق علمي، ومنطق غيبي فنحن في دروس الكيمياء والفيزياء والبيولوجي والجيولوجي والرياضيات علميون، ننهج نهج العلم الطبيعي في معالجته قضايا الكون والإنسان فإذا تحولنا إلى دروس اللغة والتاريخ والاجتماع، بدأنا نتكلم بلسان آخر لا علاقة له بمنطق العلم. لسان يطغى عليه الميل الواضح إلى تعجيز العقل وتوهين المنطق العلمي، وإرجاع أمور الحياة والإنسان إلى الغيب، وطبع عقول الناشئة بالانبهار بظواهر الطبيعة بدلاً من ربط هذه الظواهر بعللها الطبيعية، ونظام عملها، والسنن الضابطة لها. وعندما يلتقي هذان التياران في عقل المتعلّم ينجم عن التقائهما حال من التمزق الفكري، لشدة ما بين طبيعتهما من التناقض والتضاد (۱). إن الكاتب إذن يذهب إلى تنحية الوحي - بدعوى أنه غيب - في دراساتنا الإنسانية والاجتماعية ويدعو إلى إحلال المنطق المادي، وهو ما يطلق عليه (العلمي)، وإلا فسنغدوا غيبيين نصيين وكأنه يعيرنا بالوحي ونصوصه ! وليس هذا تجنّياً منا على الكاتب ولكن حديثه هنا جاء متساوقاً مع اتجاهه الفكري العام. وهنا إن كان ثمة ما يقال تعليقاً على ذلك فإنه العزاء لمثقفين مسلمين لا يرون المخرج من الأزمة الفكرية والتربوية المعاصرة إلا بسيطرة عقلية الآخر و نفسيته على تفكيرهم ومسلكهم، بحيث يقعون في شرك الاستلاب الحضاري من حيث يدرون أولا يدرون، إذ بارقة الأمل الوحيدة عندهم- هي إحلال (۱) محمد جواد رضا التيار الوظيفي، ۷۰۹ - ۰۷۱۰
Chapter Two: Section Two - Field of Knowledge - The Unseen and the Seen
If such is the case of the intellect with the unseen, then it is even more confirmed with respect to sense perception, because its weakness in comprehending those detailed matters of the unseen is manifested in what is known as sensory deception, which will be detailed in its proper place in this study, by the permission of God Almighty. But this does not conflict with the facts of science and its principles. There is an established principle among scholars that not everything that the eye does not see or the sense does not touch is ruled as non-existent. No scholar has ever claimed that the path of knowledge is confined to any of the senses, because scholars have divisions of knowledge that make part of it sensory and part non-sensory. Without that, there would be no meaning to historical studies and future predictions. It also indicates, from another angle, the process of organizing knowledge and arranging it logically. With regard to the Noble Quran, it records a huge number of non-sensory creatures, such as the angels who intervened to support the steadfast Muslims in the Battle of Hunayn: 'O you who have believed, remember the favor of God upon you when armies came to you, and We sent upon them a wind and armies you did not see. And God is ever Seeing of what you do.' [Al-Ahzab 33:9]. Also, knowledge of how the creation of the horizons and the souls began is not within the scope of sensory knowledge: 'I did not make them witness the creation of the heavens and the earth or the creation of themselves' [Al-Kahf 18:51]. And the sons of Jacob, peace be upon him, declare their inability to preserve the unseen because it is solely the prerogative of God, and how could they perceive that with their senses: 'And we testify not except by what we knew, and we were not for the unseen preservers' [Yusuf 12:81]. If that is established, it follows that the only source of knowledge in matters of the unseen is certain report (khabar yaqini) represented in revelation, which is automatically reflected in Islamic education in its cognitive aspect, as it relies on the infallible revelation as a source and method in dealing with the field of the unseen: 'Say: I only warn you by revelation' [Al-Anbiya 21:45], 'And you did not know what the Book is, nor faith, but We made it a light by which We guide whom We will of Our servants' [Ash-Shura 42:52]. There remains no meaning after that for the objector who sees that the reliance of Islamic education on revelation plants two contradictory logics in the minds of the youth: a scientific logic and an unseen-based logic. For in our lessons of chemistry, physics, biology, geology, and mathematics we are scientific, following the method of natural science in treating issues of the universe and humanity. When we turn to lessons of language, history, and sociology, we start speaking another tongue that has no relation to the logic of science. A tongue dominated by a clear tendency to incapacitate the intellect and weaken the scientific logic, and to refer the affairs of life and humanity to the unseen, and to imprint the minds of youth with awe of natural phenomena instead of linking these phenomena to their natural causes, their system of operation, and the laws governing them. When these two currents meet in the learner's mind, their meeting results in a state of intellectual fragmentation due to the extreme contradiction and opposition between their natures. The author thus goes to set aside revelation - under the pretext that it is the unseen - in our human and social studies, and calls for the replacement of material logic, which he calls (scientific), otherwise we will become scriptural unseen-based, as if he is reproaching us for revelation and its texts! This is not an exaggeration on our part against the author, but his talk here is consistent with his general intellectual direction. And here, if there is anything to say in comment, it is the consolation for Muslim intellectuals who see no way out of the contemporary intellectual and educational crisis except by the dominance of the other's mentality and psychology over their thought and conduct, such that they fall into the trap of civilizational alienation whether they realize it or not, as the only glimmer of hope for them is the replacement (1) Muhammad Jawad Rida, Al-Tayyar al-Wadhifi, 709-710.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument defending the role of revelation in knowledge, particularly concerning the unseen (ghayb), and critiquing a secular materialist approach. The author begins by noting that the intellect's weakness in grasping detailed unseen matters is confirmed by sensory deception, but this does not contradict scientific facts. Scholars have always recognized that knowledge is not limited to sensory perception; otherwise historical studies and predictions would be meaningless. The author then cites Quranic verses to support the existence of non-sensory entities (angels) and that creation itself is beyond sensory knowledge. From this, he concludes that the only source for knowledge of the unseen is certain report (khabar yaqini), i.e., revelation, which grounds Islamic education. He then refutes the objection that Islamic education creates two conflicting logics (scientific and unseen-based), arguing that the objector's claim is inconsistent with the author's own materialist tendency. The passage ends with a lament for Muslim intellectuals who fall into civilizational alienation by adopting the other's mentality.

Key Terms
الغيب
الحس
الوحي
الخبر اليقيني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the source of knowledge for matters of the unseen?
A) Sensory perception and scientific experimentation
B) Rational deduction alone
C) Certain report (khabar yaqini) from revelation
D) Historical analogies

Key Takeaway
The author establishes that knowledge is not limited to the sensory; the unseen requires a different epistemic source—revelation—and this does not conflict with science.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the implicit conditional argument in the author’s reasoning from sensory limitation to revelation as the only source. Then, using the same conditional form, analyze a similar argument from Islamic kalam: 'If human reason cannot determine the good and evil of actions without guidance, then revelation is needed to provide moral law.' Is this argument valid? Justify.
?
Critique the secular objection yourself: the objector claims that Islamic education creates two contradictory logics. Using the author’s refutation as a model, explain why this objection is inconsistent with the fact that all knowledge (including science) relies on non-sensory assumptions.

Critiquing the Claim that Revelation Contradicts Scientific Logic
Author critiques secular view that revelation conflicts with scientific logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and refute the claim that Islamic education creates conflicting logics by distinguishing between scientific methodology and materialistic philosophy.

Core Idea
Revelation does not conflict with science; it provides a broader epistemic framework that includes both the unseen and the witnessed.

In this passage, the author responds to an objection that Islamic education splits the learner's mind into two conflicting logics: scientific and religious. You will learn how to deconstruct this objection and see how the Quran itself encourages scientific inquiry within a faith-based worldview.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector's claim
Read the objector's assertion: teaching revelation alongside science creates two conflicting logics (scientific and ghaybi) leading to intellectual fragmentation.
The objector equates 'scientific logic' with materialistic logic that excludes the Unseen.
2
Unpack the underlying assumptions
The objector assumes that revelation disables reason and that scientific inquiry must be materialistic. Identify these hidden premises.
This assumption is called 'materialistic logic' (al-mantiq al-madi) in the passage.
3
Examine the author's Quranic counter-evidence
The author cites Quranic verses that encourage observation of nature and linking it to divine power. Note how the verse from Fatir (35:27-28) integrates empirical study with fear of God.
The verse calls scientists (ulama) those who fear God, showing no conflict.
4
Assess the author's conclusion about civilizational subjugation
The author argues that the real root of the objection is not logical but cultural: uncritical adoption of Western paradigms. Evaluate whether this explanation is convincing.
The concept of 'civilizational subjugation' (al-istilab al-hadari) is key to the author's critique.

الآخر بمشكلاته ما يتفق منها ومشكلاتنا وما يختلف في مواقعنا. فالنص القرآني -مثلاً- غيب شأنه في ذلك شأن النصوص المقدسة في الغرب، التي لم يحصل التنوير والتقدم إلا حين رفضها رجال العلم هناك. وعلماء الدين عندنا هـم بالضرورة رجال دين لا يختلف حالهم عن القسس والباباوات في أوروبا

الْعُلَماء ... [فاطر: ٢٧/٣٥-٢٨].
ولنا أن نتساءل هل في الدعوة إلى عظمة الله - تعالى - وبديع صنعه من خلال آياته المبثوثة في الكون ما يتعارض ودراسة السنن والعلل وتنمية الاتجاه العلمي وليس المادي الملحد ؟.
إن هذا الاستلاب حقاً أوقع الكاتب في إغفال بديهية حضارية عبر عنهـا أحد الباحثين بقوله: (لعل أهم ظاهرة في الحضارة الإسلامية أن تقدمها المادي لم ينته إلى الإلحاد والتفلت من سلطان الدين والقيم الأخلاقية والتمرد على الله - تعالى - بل كانت منضبطة في إطار الدين حتى وهي في أوجها. ويرجع ذلك
Chapter Two, Section Two: The Field of Knowledge - the Unseen and the Witnessed. In its cognitive aspect, it is based on the infallible revelation as a source and method for dealing with the field of the Unseen: 'Say, I only warn you by revelation' [Al-Anbiya 21:45], and 'You did not know what the Book is nor faith, but We made it a light by which We guide whom We will of Our servants' [Ash-Shura 42:52]. No meaning remains after that for the objector who sees that the dependence of Islamic education on revelation plants in the minds of the youth two conflicting logics: a scientific logic and a ghaybi logic. We are scientific in chemistry, physics, biology, geology, and mathematics, following the natural science approach in dealing with issues of the universe and man. Then when we move to lessons of language, history, and sociology, we start speaking with another tongue that has no relation to the logic of science. A tongue dominated by a clear tendency to disable the mind and weaken scientific logic, attributing matters of life and man to the Unseen, and imprinting the minds of the youth with amazement at natural phenomena instead of linking these phenomena to their natural causes, their system of operation, and the laws governing them. When these two currents meet in the learner's mind, a state of intellectual fragmentation results from their meeting, due to the severity of the contradiction and opposition between their natures. (1) The writer thus goes to set aside revelation - under the pretext that it is the Unseen - in our human and social studies, and calls for the substitution of materialistic logic, which he calls (scientific), otherwise we will become textual ghaybis, as if he reproaches us for revelation and its texts! This is not unfairness on our part toward the writer, but his speech here came consistent with his general intellectual direction. And here, if there is anything to say in comment on that, it is condolence for Muslim intellectuals who see no way out of the contemporary intellectual and educational crisis except through the control of the mentality and psychology of the other over their thinking and conduct, such that they fall into the trap of civilizational subjugation, knowingly or unknowingly. For the only glimmer of hope for them is the replacement of the other's problems, what agrees with our problems and what differs in our positions. The Quranic text, for example, is Unseen, just like the sacred texts in the West, which enlightenment and progress only occurred when scientists there rejected them. Our religious scholars are necessarily religious men, no different from the priests and popes in Europe and the West in general, deceiving, falsifying, and claiming holiness for themselves and their distorted books. If we continue teaching the youth science and faith together, that will split the learner into two halves, and will allow religious men to exploit that situation to be content with amazement at natural phenomena, not going beyond that to study the causes and laws governing them... (like that). The supposed question here, or in the Book of Allah Almighty - the Noble Quran - addressed to natural scientists of various specializations - without mentioning religious scholars here - what truly weakens the minds of the youth and tears their thought? Reflect on the saying of the Truth Almighty: 'Do you not see that Allah sends down rain from the sky, and We produce thereby fruits of varying colors? And in the mountains are tracts, white and red of various shades and pitch black. And among people and moving creatures and grazing livestock are likewise of various colors. Only those of His servants who have knowledge fear Allah.' [Fatir 35:27-28]. We may ask: Is there in the call to the greatness of Allah Almighty and His wonderful creation through His signs scattered in the universe anything that contradicts the study of laws and causes and the development of a scientific, not materialistic atheistic, direction? This subjugation indeed caused the writer to overlook a civilizational axiom expressed by one researcher: 'Perhaps the most important phenomenon in Islamic civilization is that its material progress did not lead to atheism, moral laxity, and rebellion against Allah Almighty, but was disciplined within the framework of religion even at its peak. That is due to...'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a critical response to a writer who argues that Islamic education, by relying on revelation, creates two conflicting logics in students: a scientific logic and a ghaybi (unseen) logic. The author begins by affirming that Islamic knowledge is based on infallible revelation, citing Quranic verses. The objector claims that in subjects like chemistry and physics, students follow natural science, but in language, history, and sociology, they shift to a discourse that disables reason and attributes everything to the Unseen, causing intellectual fragmentation. The author then interprets the objector's stance as a call to set aside revelation in human and social studies, replacing it with materialistic logic. The author laments that some Muslim intellectuals see no solution except adopting the mentality of the West, falling into civilizational subjugation. The author refutes the claim that the Quranic text is like distorted Western scriptures and that religious scholars are like priests who deceive. The author argues that teaching both science and faith does not split the learner; rather, the Quran itself encourages the study of nature and its laws, as shown in the verse from Surah Fatir. The author questions whether calling attention to God's creation contradicts scientific inquiry. Finally, the author cites a researcher noting that Islamic civilization's material progress did not lead to atheism but remained within a religious framework. The commentary follows the author's order: presenting the objection, analyzing its underlying assumptions, offering Quranic evidence, and concluding with a counterexample from Islamic history.

Key Terms

الشهادة
الوحي
المنطق المادي
الاستلاب الحضاري

A) Ignorance of the Quran
B) Civilizational subjugation
C) Scientific illiteracy
D) Overemphasis on tradition

Key Takeaway
The claim that revelation conflicts with scientific logic is a product of civilizational subjugation, not an inherent contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Using the Quranic verse from Fatir (35:27-28) as a model, construct a brief argument refuting the claim that revelation disables reason. Your argument should show how the Quran encourages the study of natural causes while maintaining a theistic worldview.

beginner

The Purpose of Existence and the Unseen
First three principles of the unseen world

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the first three principles of the unseen world and their educational implications.

Core Idea
The unseen world has rational principles that ground Islamic education.

The passage begins by setting the stage for understanding the relationship between the human knower and the unseen world. It then lists ten principles that define this relationship. The first three principles focus on the purpose of existence, the limits of human will, and the primacy of God's existence. These form the theological foundation for an Islamic worldview and directly inform the goals of Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first three principles
Read principles 1-3: existence has a good purpose, universal relationships are beyond human will, and God's existence is the most important given. Note the Quranic evidence for principle 1.
Principle 2 implies that human will does not control the laws of nature; this sets limits on human power.
2
Understand the justification for each principle
Principle 1 is justified by Quran 23:115. Principle 2 is reasoned: universal relationships (like cause-effect) are beyond human capacity. Principle 3 is the foundational belief in tawhid.
3
Connect to educational aims
Islamic education aims to produce a monotheistic human being (principle 3). The purposefulness of existence (principle 1) gives education a teleological direction. The limits on human will (principle 2) teach humility before divine order.
This shows that education is not value-neutral but grounded in metaphysical truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ضوء ما سبق لعله أضحى من الممكن تحديد نمط العلاقة التي قطباهـا الإنسان مورد المعرفة أو متلقيها، وعالم الغيب أي الموضوع المعروف هاهنا، فيما يمكن تسميته بمباديء عالم الغيب ومعطياته بالنسبة للإنسان. وقد سعى أحد الباحثين لمحاولة تحديد مبادئ عالم الغيب بما يمكن تلخيصه على النحو التالي: 1 - الوجود ذو غاية خيرة: ﴿ أَفَحَسِبْتُمْ أَنَّمَا خَلَقْنَاكُمْ عَبَثًا وَأَنَّكُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا تُرْجَعُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١١٥/٢٣]. وهذا يحدّد الهدف العام من الوجود في صورة هذا الهدف الغائي. ۲- علاقات الوجود الكلية غير الخاضعة لإرادة الإنسان فيما وراء طاقته الإنسانية. ۳- وجود الله تعالى يمثل أهم معطى في عالم الغيب بالنسبة إلى الإنسان. وعلى هذا الأساس فإن التربية الإسلامية تهدف إلى إخراج الإنسان الموحد. ٤ - الدار الآخرة تمثل محصلة حسابية وجزائية نهائية لما قدمه الإنسان في الدنيا. وفي هذا تربية على الرقابة الذاتية للفرد. ۵- الدنيا دار عمل وإصلاح . ومن هذا المنطلق فإن علاقة الإنسان بالدنيا علاقة ابتلاء واختبار. ٦- الإرادة الإنسانية وفق علم الله أمر وقد أوكل إليها القيام بمهام الخلافة. وأداء الخلافة يتطلب شرائط مهارية يجب أن يسعى المنهج بجميع عناصره لبلورتها. ۷- الهداية والضلالة في حياة الإنسان مصير فردي يسبق في علم الله، حين وهب الإنسان حرية الاختيار. ولذلك فلا معنى للتربية على التواكل والجبرية ومظاهر العجز كافة. ۸- خلق الله الإنسان ووهبه العقل والعلم، وكرّمه مركز الخلافة في الأرض، وجعل من العلم وحرية الإرادة عاملا مميزا له على سائر الكائنات، حيث يقوم بمسؤوليته، ولكنه إن ضلّ وفسد تردى إلى أسفل سافلين. وتتضمن هذه الإرادة حرية المتعلم، واستقلالية قراره في اختيار التخصص المناسب لقدراته وطاقاته الإبداعية الكفيلة بانطلاقه نحو جملة الأنشطة والتفاعلات التي يجد نفسه فيها راغباً متفاعلاً مبدعاً. ۹- الكون والكائنات مفطورة على سنن وقوانين وأسباب وحتى تتحقق الغايات لابد من تحقيق الأفعال والأعمال ليرتبط السبب بالمسبب، وتكون الأمور كما أرادها لها خالقها. وفي هذا شحذ لعقلية المتعلم، وتنظيم منطقي لمعارفه، وتربية له على النظام والانضباط في الفكر والسلوك. ١٠- بعد بذل الأسباب تعفى مسؤولية الإنسان فيتوكل على الله، صاحب الأمر، وعالم الغيب، ومسيّر الكون إيماناً وثقة بحكمته. وهذا يقضي على التعارض الموهوم بين التوكل وبذل السبب.
In light of the above, perhaps it has become possible to identify the pattern of relationship whose two poles are the human being, the source or recipient of knowledge, and the world of the unseen, i.e., the known subject here, in what can be called the principles of the world of the unseen and its givens with respect to the human being. One researcher sought to determine the principles of the world of the unseen in what can be summarized as follows: 1 - Existence has a good purpose: {Did you then think that We created you in vain and that to Us you would not be returned?} [Al-Mu'minun: 23:115]. This defines the general purpose of existence in the form of this teleological goal. 2 - The universal relationships of existence are not subject to human will beyond his human capacity. 3 - The existence of God Almighty represents the most important given in the world of the unseen for the human being. On this basis, Islamic education aims to produce a monotheistic human being. 4 - The hereafter represents a final accounting and recompense for what the human being has done in this world. In this is a cultivation of self-monitoring for the individual. 5 - This world is a realm of work and reform. From this perspective, the human being's relationship with the world is a relationship of trial and test. 6 - Human will is according to God's knowledge, and the responsibilities of vicegerency have been entrusted to it. Performing vicegerency requires skill conditions that the curriculum must strive with all its elements to crystallize. 7 - Guidance and misguidance in human life are an individual destiny preceded in God's knowledge, when He granted the human being freedom of choice. Therefore, there is no meaning to education based on fatalism, compulsion, and all manifestations of helplessness. 8 - God created the human being, endowed him with intellect and knowledge, honored him with the position of vicegerent on earth, and made knowledge and free will a distinguishing factor for him over other creatures, whereby he fulfills his responsibility. But if he goes astray and becomes corrupt, he sinks to the lowest of the low. This will includes the learner's freedom and the independence of his decision in choosing the specialization appropriate to his abilities and creative energies, enabling him to launch into a range of activities and interactions in which he finds himself willing, interactive, and creative. 9 - The universe and creatures are created with laws, regulations, and causes. For ends to be achieved, actions and deeds must be accomplished so that the cause is linked to the effect, and matters become as their Creator intended for them. In this is a sharpening of the learner's mentality, a logical organization of his knowledge, and a cultivation of order and discipline in thought and behavior. 10 - After taking the means, the human being's responsibility is discharged, and he places his trust in God, the Owner of the matter, the Knower of the unseen, and the Director of the universe, with faith and confidence in His wisdom. This eliminates the illusory contradiction between trust in God and taking the means.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition enumerating ten foundational principles of the unseen world (ghayb) and their relevance to Islamic education. The author begins by setting the context: after previous discussion, it becomes possible to define the relationship between the human being (the knower) and the unseen world (the known). The principles are then listed as determined by a researcher. Each principle is briefly explained. Principle 1 states that existence has a good purpose, citing Quran 23:115 to reject the notion of creation in vain. Principle 2 points out that the universal relationships of existence transcend human will. Principle 3 emphasizes the existence of God as the primary given of the unseen, forming the basis for raising a monotheistic individual. Principle 4 highlights the afterlife as a final accountability, fostering self-monitoring. Principle 5 characterizes this world as a place of work and reform, making human life a trial. Principle 6 notes that human will operates within divine knowledge and is entrusted with vicegerency, requiring skill development. Principle 7 affirms that guidance and misguidance are individual destinies alongside human free choice, thus rejecting fatalistic education. Principle 8 describes the creation of humans with intellect and free will, their vicegerency, and the consequences of deviation. Principle 9 states that the universe operates on laws and causes, linking cause and effect, which sharpens logical thinking. Principle 10 resolves the apparent contradiction between relying on God and taking means: after exerting effort, one trusts in God. The passage thus integrates theological beliefs with educational philosophy, grounding pedagogy in Islamic worldview.

الشهادة
الوجود ذو غاية خيرة

B) The universal relationships are subject to human will.
C) Existence has no purpose.
D) Human will is the ultimate cause of everything.

Key Takeaway
The first three principles establish that existence has purpose, human will is limited, and God's existence is central—forming the theological foundation of Islamic education.

Accountability and Human Responsibility
Principles 4-6 on accountability and responsibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how principles 4-6 (afterlife, world as trial, human will within divine knowledge) form a framework for moral responsibility in Islamic education.

Core Idea
The afterlife as ultimate accountability makes self-monitoring central to education.

Principles 4-6 address the temporal and eternal dimensions of human life. The afterlife is presented as a final reckoning, this world as a place of trial, and human will as the instrument for vicegerency. Together, they create a system of moral responsibility that Islamic education must cultivate.

Guided Path
1
List principles 4, 5, and 6
Principle 4: The hereafter is a final accounting and recompense. Principle 5: This world is a realm of work and reform, a trial. Principle 6: Human will is according to divine knowledge and entrusted with vicegerency.
2
Analyze the logical connection between them
The world is a test (5), the result is judged in the afterlife (4), and the test is conducted through free will (6). Thus, human actions have eternal consequences, necessitating self-monitoring and skill development.
This triad underlines personal accountability.
3
Derive educational implications
Education must foster self-monitoring (muraqaba), prepare for the trial of life, and develop skills required for vicegerency (khilafa). The curriculum should therefore include ethical training and practical competencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

D) It has no purpose.

Key Takeaway
Principles 4-6 create a coherent system: the world as a test, the afterlife as judgment, and human will as the means to fulfill vicegerency—all of which shape the goals of Islamic education.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Explain how Principle 4 (afterlife as final accounting) promotes self-monitoring in students.
?
Describe the relationship between human will and divine knowledge as stated in Principle 6, and why the curriculum must develop skills for vicegerency.

Free Will, Guidance, and Human Potential
Principles 7-8 on free will and human potential

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the balance between divine destiny and human free choice as expressed in principles 7-8 and its educational consequences.

Core Idea
Humans are given free will and intellect, so fatalism is rejected in Islamic education.

Principles 7 and 8 delve into the dynamics of guidance and misguidance, free will, and human potential. Principle 7 affirms that guidance is an individual destiny while still granting freedom of choice, thereby rejecting fatalistic education. Principle 8 elaborates on the honor of vicegerency, the gift of intellect and free will, and the consequences of deviation. These principles underscore the dignity of the learner and the need for an education that fosters responsibility and creativity.

Guided Path
1
Understand Principle 7
Guidance and misguidance are individual destinies known to God, but humans are given free choice. Therefore, education must reject fatalism (tawakkul, jabriyya) and helplessness.
This refutes predestinarian views that undermine educational effort.
2
Understand Principle 8
God created humans with intellect, knowledge, and free will, making them vicegerents. If they go astray, they fall to the lowest. The passage emphasizes learner freedom and independence in choosing specialization.
This promotes personalized education based on abilities and creativity.
3
Connect to educational practice
Education should emphasize human responsibility, encourage free choice within Islamic boundaries, and develop each learner's unique creative potential. Fatalistic teaching is counterproductive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ضوء ما سبق لعله أضحى من الممكن تحديد نمط العلاقة التي قطباهـا الإنسان مورد المعرفة أو متلقيها، وعالم الغيب أي الموضوع المعروف هاهنا، فيما يمكن تسميته بمباديء عالم الغيب ومعطياته بالنسبة للإنسان. وقد سعى أحد الباحثين لمحاولة تحديد مبادئ عالم الغيب بما يمكن تلخيصه على النحو التالي: 1 - الوجود ذو غاية خيرة: ﴿ أَفَحَسِبْتُمْ أَنَّمَا خَلَقْنَاكُمْ عَبَثًا وَأَنَّكُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا تُرْجَعُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١١٥/٢٣]. وهذا يحدّد الهدف العام من الوجود في صورة هذا الهدف الغائي. ۲- علاقات الوجود الكلية غير الخاضعة لإرادة الإنسان فيما وراء طاقته الإنسانية. ۳- وجود الله تعالى يمثل أهم معطى في عالم الغيب بالنسبة إلى الإنسان. وعلى هذا الأساس فإن التربية الإسلامية تهدف إلى إخراج الإنسان الموحد. ٤ - الدار الآخرة تمثل محصلة حسابية وجزائية نهائية لما قدمه الإنسان في الدنيا. وفي هذا تربية على الرقابة الذاتية للفرد. ۵- الدنيا دار عمل وإصلاح . ومن هذا المنطلق فإن علاقة الإنسان بالدنيا علاقة ابتلاء واختبار. ٦- الإرادة الإنسانية وفق علم الله أمر وقد أوكل إليها القيام بمهام الخلافة. وأداء الخلافة يتطلب شرائط مهارية يجب أن يسعى المنهج بجميع عناصره لبلورتها. ۷- الهداية والضلالة في حياة الإنسان مصير فردي يسبق في علم الله، حين وهب الإنسان حرية الاختيار. ولذلك فلا معنى للتربية على التواكل والجبرية ومظاهر العجز كافة. ۸- خلق الله الإنسان ووهبه العقل والعلم، وكرّمه مركز الخلافة في الأرض، وجعل من العلم وحرية الإرادة عاملا مميزا له على سائر الكائنات، حيث يقوم بمسؤوليته، ولكنه إن ضلّ وفسد تردى إلى أسفل سافلين. وتتضمن هذه الإرادة حرية المتعلم، واستقلالية قراره في اختيار التخصص المناسب لقدراته وطاقاته الإبداعية الكفيلة بانطلاقه نحو جملة الأنشطة والتفاعلات التي يجد نفسه فيها راغباً متفاعلاً مبدعاً. ۹- الكون والكائنات مفطورة على سنن وقوانين وأسباب وحتى تتحقق الغايات لابد من تحقيق الأفعال والأعمال ليرتبط السبب بالمسبب، وتكون الأمور كما أرادها لها خالقها. وفي هذا شحذ لعقلية المتعلم، وتنظيم منطقي لمعارفه، وتربية له على النظام والانضباط في الفكر والسلوك. ١٠- بعد بذل الأسباب تعفى مسؤولية الإنسان فيتوكل على الله، صاحب الأمر، وعالم الغيب، ومسيّر الكون إيماناً وثقة بحكمته. وهذا يقضي على التعارض الموهوم بين التوكل وبذل السبب.
In light of the above, perhaps it has become possible to identify the pattern of relationship whose two poles are the human being, the source or recipient of knowledge, and the world of the unseen, i.e., the known subject here, in what can be called the principles of the world of the unseen and its givens with respect to the human being. One researcher sought to determine the principles of the world of the unseen in what can be summarized as follows: 1 - Existence has a good purpose: {Did you then think that We created you in vain and that to Us you would not be returned?} [Al-Mu'minun: 23:115]. This defines the general purpose of existence in the form of this teleological goal. 2 - The universal relationships of existence are not subject to human will beyond his human capacity. 3 - The existence of God Almighty represents the most important given in the world of the unseen for the human being. On this basis, Islamic education aims to produce a monotheistic human being. 4 - The hereafter represents a final accounting and recompense for what the human being has done in this world. In this is a cultivation of self-monitoring for the individual. 5 - This world is a realm of work and reform. From this perspective, the human being's relationship with the world is a relationship of trial and test. 6 - Human will is according to God's knowledge, and the responsibilities of vicegerency have been entrusted to it. Performing vicegerency requires skill conditions that the curriculum must strive with all its elements to crystallize. 7 - Guidance and misguidance in human life are an individual destiny preceded in God's knowledge, when He granted the human being freedom of choice. Therefore, there is no meaning to education based on fatalism, compulsion, and all manifestations of helplessness. 8 - God created the human being, endowed him with intellect and knowledge, honored him with the position of vicegerent on earth, and made knowledge and free will a distinguishing factor for him over other creatures, whereby he fulfills his responsibility. But if he goes astray and becomes corrupt, he sinks to the lowest of the low. This will includes the learner's freedom and the independence of his decision in choosing the specialization appropriate to his abilities and creative energies, enabling him to launch into a range of activities and interactions in which he finds himself willing, interactive, and creative. 9 - The universe and creatures are created with laws, regulations, and causes. For ends to be achieved, actions and deeds must be accomplished so that the cause is linked to the effect, and matters become as their Creator intended for them. In this is a sharpening of the learner's mentality, a logical organization of his knowledge, and a cultivation of order and discipline in thought and behavior. 10 - After taking the means, the human being's responsibility is discharged, and he places his trust in God, the Owner of the matter, the Knower of the unseen, and the Director of the universe, with faith and confidence in His wisdom. This eliminates the illusory contradiction between trust in God and taking the means.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition enumerating ten foundational principles of the unseen world (ghayb) and their relevance to Islamic education. The author begins by setting the context: after previous discussion, it becomes possible to define the relationship between the human being (the knower) and the unseen world (the known). The principles are then listed as determined by a researcher. Each principle is briefly explained. Principle 1 states that existence has a good purpose, citing Quran 23:115 to reject the notion of creation in vain. Principle 2 points out that the universal relationships of existence transcend human will. Principle 3 emphasizes the existence of God as the primary given of the unseen, forming the basis for raising a monotheistic individual. Principle 4 highlights the afterlife as a final accountability, fostering self-monitoring. Principle 5 characterizes this world as a place of work and reform, making human life a trial. Principle 6 notes that human will operates within divine knowledge and is entrusted with vicegerency, requiring skill development. Principle 7 affirms that guidance and misguidance are individual destinies alongside human free choice, thus rejecting fatalistic education. Principle 8 describes the creation of humans with intellect and free will, their vicegerency, and the consequences of deviation. Principle 9 states that the universe operates on laws and causes, linking cause and effect, which sharpens logical thinking. Principle 10 resolves the apparent contradiction between relying on God and taking means: after exerting effort, one trusts in God. The passage thus integrates theological beliefs with educational philosophy, grounding pedagogy in Islamic worldview.

حرية الاختيار
الخلافة
حرية المتعلم

Causality and Trust in God
Principles 9-10 on causality and trust

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the complementarity between taking means and trusting God as presented in principles 9-10.

Core Idea
Islamic education cultivates both logical cause-effect reasoning and sincere tawakkul.

The final two principles address the relationship between natural causality and reliance on God. Principle 9 states that the universe operates on fixed laws and causes, and that education should sharpen logical thinking. Principle 10 resolves the apparent contradiction: after exhausting means, one trusts in God. Together, they teach a balanced approach combining effort and faith.

Guided Path
1
Examine Principle 9
The universe and creatures are created with laws, regulations, and causes. To achieve goals, actions must be performed to link cause and effect. This sharpens mentality and organizes knowledge.
This justifies the teaching of natural sciences and logical thinking.
2
Examine Principle 10
After taking the means, human responsibility is discharged, and one trusts in God. This eliminates the illusory contradiction between tawakkul and taking means.
Tawakkul is not fatalism but active reliance after effort.
3
Synthesize the educational implication
Education must teach students to take effective means (asbab) while simultaneously cultivating trust in God. Both are complementary, not contradictory.
This prevents two extremes: neglecting effort or neglecting dependence on God.

The Quranic Classification of Knowledge: Shahada and Ghayb
Author explains the Quranic classification of knowledge into witnessed and unseen domains and their interdependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Quranic concepts of shahada (witnessed) and ghayb (unseen) and explain their complementary relationship.

Core Idea
The Quran divides knowledge into two complementary fields: the witnessed and the unseen.

The Quranic worldview recognizes that human knowledge encompasses both the observable physical world and the metaphysical unseen. This lesson explores how these two domains are defined in the Quran and how they work together to guide the believer towards certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two domains
In the Arabic passage, locate the terms al-shahada and al-ghayb. What realms do they refer to? Look for descriptions of what each includes.
Shahada is the physical world; ghayb is the unseen metaphysical realm.
2
Examine what falls under shahada
The passage gives examples like trees, deserts, galaxies, and everything sensed. List these and note their common feature.
These are all objects of sense perception.
3
Understand the complementary nature
The author says the witnessed field is 'the other complementary part' of the unseen. What does that mean for knowledge acquisition?
The two are not isolated; one completes the other.
4
Connect to Quranic verses
The author cites verses that mention both domains. How do these verses link the two?
Verses often point to signs in creation to affirm the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
والحق أن هذا التقسيم ليس خاصاً بالمسلمين وحدهم، فقد سار عليه فلاسفة اليونان كذلك حيث بدؤوا بالكون، الذي هو أول ما يقع عليه بصر الإنسان. أما الإنسان فمحور التفلسف عند سقراط. وكانت قضية الألوهية هي ثالثة قضايا التفلسف التي اكتملت في فلسفة أفلاطون وأرسطو (۱) وهذا الذي يسميه الفلاسفة عالم الطبيعة، الذي يضم الشجر والورود والصحاري والمجرات والنجوم، وكذا كل ما يراه الإنسان أو يشمه أو يحسه عموماً هو ما يسميه القرآن عالم الشهادة (٢).
وعلى هذا فإن ميدان الشهادة - من الناحية التربوية - يرتكز في فلسفته على الاهتمام بطاقات المتعلم، وتوجيهها في كلا الميدانين، باعتبارهما معاً الشطر الآخر المكمل لميدان الغيب.
العلاقة بينهما
ونحن نلمس أن ثمة علاقة جدلية قائمة بين ميداني الآفاق والأنفس من خلال جملة من النصوص القرآنية، ومنها: {وما أَشْهَدْتُهُمْ خَلْقَ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَلَا خَلْقَ أَنْفُسِهِمْ وَمَا كُنتُ مُتَّخِذَ الْمُضِلَّينَ عَضُداً} [الكهف: 51/18] {أَوَلَمْ يَتَفَكَّرُوا فِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ ما خَلَقَ اللهُ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَمَا بَيْنَهُما إِلا بِالْحَقِّ وَأَجَلٍ مُسَمَّى وَإِنَّ كَثِيراً مِنَ النَّاسِ بِلِقَاءِ رَبِّهِمْ لَكَافِرُونَ} [الروم: 8/30] {وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ خَلْقُ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافُ أَلْسِنَتِكُمْ وَأَلْوَانِكُمْ إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لآياتِ لِلْعالِمِينَ} [الروم: 22/30] (۱) حمدي زقزوق، الدين والفلسفة، 17 . (٢) مرتضى المطهري، معرفة القرآن، 173 - 174 .
وَفِي الْأَرْضِ آيات لِلْمُوقِنِينَ، وَفِي أَنْفُسِكُمْ أَفَلا تُبْصِرُونَ [الذاريات: 20/51 - 21]. وإِنَّ فِي السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتٍ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَفِي خَلْقِكُمْ وَمَا يَبُثُّ مِنْ دابَّةٍ آيات لِقَوْمٍ يُوقِنُونَ، وَاخْتِلافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَمَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِنْ رِزْقِ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّياحِ آيَاتٌ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ تِلْكَ آيات الله نقلُوها عَلَيْكَ بِالْحَقِّ فَبِأَيِّ حَدِيثٍ بَعْدَ اللهِ وَآيَاتِهِ يُؤْمِنُونَ [الجانية: 3/45 - 6] .
إن فحوى تلك الآيات يشير إلى ميدان عالم الشهادة بقسميه الآفاق والأنفس. الآفاق تلك التي تتناول ظواهر الكون ومخلوقاته وطاقاته وقوانينه، والأنفس تلك التي تتناول الإنسان بمختلف عناصره ومظاهره. وتتجلى مظاهر العلاقة الجدلية بينهما في هذا التلازم المشير إلى الإبداع في الخلق، دليل وجود الخالق البديع سبحانه.
(إن القرآن الكريم يرينا الترابط والتفاعل بين الظاهرات الطبيعية المختلفة، وبينها كلها وبين الإنسان فالسحاب يؤدي إلى المطر، والمطر ينبت الزرع والشجر، وهذا يغذي الحيوان والإنسان والإنسان يسخر الكثير من المخلوقات. فعليه أن يرى علاقة ذلك بخالق الكون ومسيّره) (۱) .
وهذا يدل بالتأكيد على أن فلسفة التربية الإسلامية فلسفة مؤمنة توحيدية، تقوم على المواءمة بين العلم والدين، أو التوحيد والكون، من غير حدوث تناقض، أو نشوء اضطراب. ومن هنا تميّزت التربية الإسلامية باعتمادها عناصر التقوى والورع والإيمان مقومات رئيسة لأي مناهج (۱) محمد فاضل الجمالي، نحو توحيد الفكر التربوي، 90 - 91 ، وتربية الإنسان الجديد، 119 - 120 .
Chapter Two: Section Two - The Field of Knowledge - The Unseen and the Witnessed
And the truth is that this division is not specific to Muslims alone; the Greek philosophers also followed it as they began with the universe, which is the first thing that falls upon human sight. As for man, he is the axis of philosophizing according to Socrates. And the issue of divinity was the third issue of philosophizing that was completed in the philosophy of Plato and Aristotle. (1) And this is what philosophers call the natural world, which includes trees, flowers, deserts, galaxies, and stars, as well as everything that man sees, smells, or senses in general, is what the Qur'an calls the witnessed world (2).
And accordingly, the field of the witnessed - from an educational perspective - is based in its philosophy on paying attention to the learner's potentials and directing them in both fields, considering both together as the other complementary part of the field of the unseen.
The Relationship Between Them
And we perceive that there is a dialectical relationship existing between the fields of the horizons (afaq) and the selves (anfus) through a number of Qur'anic texts, including: {And I did not make them witness the creation of the heavens and the earth nor the creation of themselves, and I would not take the misleaders as assistants} [Al-Kahf: 51/18] {Do they not reflect within themselves? God created not the heavens and the earth and what is between them except with truth and for a specified term, but many of the people, in the meeting with their Lord, are disbelievers} [Ar-Rum: 8/30] {And of His signs is the creation of the heavens and the earth and the diversity of your languages and your colors. Indeed in that are signs for those who know} [Ar-Rum: 22/30] (1) Hamdi Zakzouk, Religion and Philosophy, 17. (2) Murtadha al-Mutahhari, Knowing the Qur'an, 173-174.
{And on the earth are signs for the certain [in faith], and in yourselves. Then will you not see?} [Adh-Dhariyat: 20-21/51]. {And indeed in the heavens and the earth are signs for the believers. And in your creation and what He disperses of moving creatures are signs for people who are certain [in faith]. And [in] the alternation of night and day and [in] what God sends down from the sky of provision and gives life thereby to the earth after its lifelessness and [in] the directing of the winds are signs for people who reason. These are the verses of God We recite to you in truth. Then in what statement after God and His verses will they believe?} [Al-Jathiya: 3-6/45].
Indeed, the purport of those verses indicates the field of the witnessed world in its two divisions: the horizons and the selves. The horizons are those that deal with the phenomena of the universe, its creatures, energies, and laws. And the selves are those that deal with man in his various elements and manifestations. And the manifestations of the dialectical relationship between them appear in this interdependence indicating creativity in creation, evidence of the existence of the Creator, the Originator, glorified be He.
(Indeed, the Noble Qur'an shows us the interconnection and interaction between different natural phenomena, and between all of them and man. So clouds lead to rain, rain grows crops and trees, this feeds animals and man, and man harnesses many creatures. He must see the relationship of that to the Creator of the universe and its Manager) (1).
And this certainly indicates that the philosophy of Islamic education is a believing monotheistic philosophy, based on harmony between science and religion, or monotheism and the universe, without any contradiction or disturbance arising. Hence, Islamic education is distinguished by its adoption of the elements of piety, devotion, and faith as basic components for any curricula (1) Muhammad Fadil al-Jamali, Towards Unification of Educational Thought, 90-91, and The Education of the New Human, 119-120.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition of the Quranic division of knowledge into two complementary fields: the 'witnessed' (al-shahada) and the 'unseen' (al-ghayb). The author begins by noting that this division is not unique to Islam; Greek philosophers also began with the observable universe. He then identifies three major philosophical questions: the cosmos, man, and divinity, with the Greeks focusing first on the cosmos. The Quran calls the physical world the 'witnessed world' (al-shahada). From an educational perspective, the field of the witnessed involves engaging the learner's potentials and directing them towards both fields, as the witnessed complements the unseen.

Next, the author discusses the relationship between the two fields, describing it as dialectical (jadaliyya). He supports this with several Quranic verses that link contemplation of the external universe (afaq) and the inner self (anfus) to faith in God. The verses from Surat al-Kahf, al-Rum, and others emphasize that signs of God are found both in the heavens/earth and within human beings.

The author then elaborates on the two subdivisions of the witnessed world: 'afaq' (horizons, external phenomena) and 'anfus' (selves, human aspects). The dialectical relationship between them points to the creativity of creation and serves as evidence for the existence of the Creator.

Finally, the author cites a quote about the Quran showing interconnectedness in nature, and concludes that Islamic educational philosophy is monotheistic, harmonizing science and religion without contradiction. It is distinguished by its foundation in piety, devotion, and faith as key components of curricula. The footnotes provide references to contemporary works on philosophy and education.

Key Terms
الغيب
الشهادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the witnessed world (al-shahada) and the unseen (al-ghayb)?
A) They are completely separate and independent.
B) The witnessed is the foundation, the unseen is derivative.
C) They are complementary, with the witnessed being the other part of the unseen.
D) The unseen is the only true reality; the witnessed is illusion.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic classification of knowledge into shahada and ghayb establishes a unified epistemology where the observable world complements the unseen realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the definitions from the passage, classify the following as shahada or ghayb: (a) the resurrection, (b) the water cycle, (c) the human nafs (soul).
?
Find one Quranic verse not quoted in the passage that mentions both the heavens and the self, and explain how it demonstrates the complementarity.

beginner
5 min
The Dialectical Relationship Between Afaq and Anfus
Author explains the Quranic classification of knowledge into witnessed and unseen domains and their interdependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two sub-domains of the witnessed world (afaq and anfus) and describe how their dialectical relationship points to the Creator.

Core Idea
Afaq (external horizons) and anfus (inner selves) together reveal the Creator through their interrelation.

The Quran repeatedly calls believers to reflect on both the universe and themselves. This lesson unpacks the two subdivisions of the witnessed world—the external horizons (afaq) and the inner selves (anfus)—and shows how their mutual relationship provides evidence for God's existence and unity.

Guided Path
1
Define afaq and anfus
From the passage, afaq are phenomena of the universe; anfus are human elements. Note the examples given: afaq includes creatures, energies, laws; anfus includes various human aspects.
Both are subdivisions of the witnessed world.
2
Examine the dialectical relationship
The author says there is a 'dialectical relationship' between them. Look at the Qur'anic verses that link both: they often mention heavens/earth and the self together.
Dialectical means interactive and mutually reinforcing.
3
Identify the evidence for the Creator
The passage says their interdependence indicates 'creativity in creation' and is evidence of the Creator. How does studying both lead to this conclusion?
The order and interconnection point to a Creator.
4
Apply to Islamic education
The author concludes that Islamic education harmonizes science and religion. How does the relationship between afaq and anfus support a unified educational philosophy?
Education should integrate both empirical and spiritual dimensions.

الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
والحق أن هذا التقسيم ليس خاصاً بالمسلمين وحدهم، فقد سار عليه فلاسفة اليونان كذلك حيث بدؤوا بالكون، الذي هو أول ما يقع عليه بصر الإنسان. أما الإنسان فمحور التفلسف عند سقراط. وكانت قضية الألوهية هي ثالثة قضايا التفلسف التي اكتملت في فلسفة أفلاطون وأرسطو (۱) وهذا الذي يسميه الفلاسفة عالم الطبيعة، الذي يضم الشجر والورود والصحاري والمجرات والنجوم، وكذا كل ما يراه الإنسان أو يشمه أو يحسه عموماً هو ما يسميه القرآن عالم الشهادة (٢).
وعلى هذا فإن ميدان الشهادة - من الناحية التربوية - يرتكز في فلسفته على الاهتمام بطاقات المتعلم، وتوجيهها في كلا الميدانين، باعتبارهما معاً الشطر الآخر المكمل لميدان الغيب.

According to the passage, what do the manifestations of the dialectical relationship between the horizons and the selves indicate?

?

?

intermediate

The Epistemic Function of Cosmic Signs (Ayat al-Afaq)
Author explains the role of cosmic signs in Islamic epistemology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of cosmic signs as a source of knowledge in Islamic epistemology and explain how they complement revelation.

Core Idea
The universe is a living revelation that provides empirical knowledge alongside the Quran.

In Islamic epistemology, knowledge comes from both revelation and the universe. The Quran calls the phenomena of nature 'ayat' (signs) just like its own verses. This lesson unpacks how the cosmos functions as a 'field of knowledge' (midan al-ma'rifa) that supplies laws and theories, fulfilling an educational purpose. Understanding this tool helps you appreciate the empirical basis of Islamic science and the integration of observation with faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term 'Ayat al-Afaq'
Find the term in the Arabic passage and note its meaning: cosmic signs in the horizons related to astronomy, night/day, sun/moon. The passage emphasizes they are not random but functional.
2
Recognize the epistemological claim
The author states that the field of horizons is a 'fundamental source of cognitive content' providing laws and theories from nature. This establishes the cosmos as a source of valid knowledge.
3
Connect to the concept of 'taskhir'
The harmony between creation and Creator leads the intellect to benefit, achieving subjugation (taskhir) for humanity. This shows the practical utility of cosmic knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
وتربوياً فإن هذا المعنى يتضمن اعتماد ميدان الآفاق مصدراً أساسياً من مصادر المحتوى المعرفي من حيث تزويده بالمعارف الكونية المشتملة على القوانين والنظريات المنبثقة من عناصر الطبيعة.
إن آيات الآفاق ذات الصلة بالفلك وحركة الليل والنهار والشمس والقمر قائمة وفق مفهوم وظيفي، محدّد الأدوار مرسوم التخصصات لكل أجزاء هذا الكون، ولكنها في كل هذه الأجزاء، وفي جميع تلك الحركات تسعى لتوكيد حقيقة الانسجام بينها وبين خالقها سبحانه
وهذا يلبي عنصراً آخر مهماً من عناصر المحتوى الدراسي وهـو وظيفية المحتوى، إذ إن المحتوى المنشود ليس مجرد كـم معـرفي خـال مـن الأهداف الوظيفية، بل هو محتوى عملي، ذو مردود إيجابي فعّال، على صعيد الواقع التربوي والاجتماعي العام كما نلمس ذلك في هاتين الآيتين - على سبيل المثال: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي جَعَلَ الشَّمْسَ ضِياءً وَالْقَمَرَ نُوراً وَقَدَّرَهُ مَنازِلَ لِتَعْلَمُوا عَدَدَ السِّنِينَ وَالْحِساب ما خَلَقَ اللهُ ذَلِكَ إِلَّا بِالْحَقِّ يُفَصِّلُ الآيَاتِ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [يونس: ٥/١٠]. هُوَ الَّذِي جَعَلَ لَكُمُ اللَّيْلَ لِتَسْكُنُوا فِيهِ وَالنَّهَارَ مُبْصِراً إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لآياتتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَسْمَعُونَ ﴾ [يونس: ٦٧/١٠].
إن هذا الانسجام بين عناصر الخلق وبارئها الخالق - سبحانه - يأخذ بالعقول للإفادة من تلك العناصر كلّها، وذلك لتحقيق عملية التسخير المهيئة للإنسان الشق الآخر المكوّن لعالم (الشهادة وذلك إن كان في عناصر الخلق العلوية فإنه في الأرض أيضاً، كما في مثل هذه الآيات:
﴿هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ لَكُمْ ما فِي الأَرْضِ جَمِيعاً ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى إِلَى السَّمَاءِ فَسَوَاهُنَّ سَبْعَ سَماواتِ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٩/٢)
أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ سَخَّرَ لَكُمْ ما فِي الْأَرْضِ وَالْفُلْكَ تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِأَمْرِهِ وَيُمْسِكُ السَّمَاءَ أَنْ تَقَعَ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ بِالنَّاسِ لَرَؤُوفٌ رَحِيمٌ [الحج: ٦٥/٢٢].
﴿وَاللهُ أَنْزَلَ مِنَ السَّماء ماءً فَأَحْيا بهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَةً لِقَوْمٍ يَسْمَعُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ٦٥/١٦].
وهذا يؤكد حقيقة الفلسفة المؤمنة التي تقوم عليها التربية الإسلامية في نظريتها المعرفية.
من أهداف آيات الآفاق
أما الهدف الغائي من وراء ذلك كله فالوصول إلى الحقيقة القرآنية: ... حَتى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ الْحَقُّ ﴾ [فصلت: ٥٣/٤١].
ومعرفة آياته : وَقُلِ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ سَيُرِيكُمْ آيَاتِهِ فَتَعْرِفُونَها ﴾ [النمل: ٩٣/٢٧]. ويندرج هذا في إطار الأهداف العامة لنظرية المعرفة في القرآن ومضامينها التربوية.
وأما الأهداف الفرعية فحسبنا هنا الإشارة إلى أن القرآن إذ يهتم بآيات الآفاق المتعلقة بإعمال قوى العقل مثلاً - فإنه يدعو الإنسان بوضوح إلى التعلم عن طريق ملاحظته للأشياء، وتجربته العملية في الحياة، وعن طريق التفاعل مع الكون، ومافيه من المخلوقات والأحداث وذلك بمختلف الطرائق الحسية أو العقلية.
Chapter Two, Section Two: The Field of Knowledge - The Unseen and the Witnessed.
Educationally, this meaning entails adopting the field of horizons as a fundamental source of the cognitive content, in terms of providing it with cosmic knowledge containing the laws and theories emanating from the elements of nature.
The verses of the horizons related to astronomy, the movement of night and day, the sun and the moon, are based on a functional concept, with defined roles and prescribed specializations for all parts of this universe, but in all these parts, and in all those movements, they seek to affirm the reality of harmony between them and their Creator, glory be to Him.
And this fulfills another important element of the curricular content, which is the functionality of content, for the desired content is not merely a cognitive quantity devoid of functional objectives, but rather a practical content with effective positive return on the level of educational and social reality in general, as we perceive that in these two verses - for example: [Yunus 10:5] 'It is He who made the sun a shining light and the moon a reflected light and determined for it phases - that you may know the number of years and account. Allah did not create that except in truth. He details the signs for a people who know.' and [Yunus 10:67] 'It is He who made the night for you that you may rest therein and the day giving sight. Indeed in that are signs for a people who listen.'
Indeed, this harmony between the elements of creation and their Creator - glory be to Him - takes the intellects to benefit from all those elements, and that is to achieve the process of subjugation prepared for man, the other component of the world of witnessing. And whether it is in the celestial elements of creation, it is also on earth, as in such verses: 
[Al-Baqarah 2:29] 'It is He who created for you all that is on earth. Then He directed Himself to the heaven, and fashioned it into seven heavens. And He is Knowing of all things.'
[Al-Hajj 22:65] 'Do you not see that Allah has subjected to you whatever is on the earth and the ships which run through the sea by His command? And He restrains the sky from falling upon the earth, unless by His permission. Indeed Allah, to the people, is Kind and Merciful.'
[An-Nahl 16:65] 'And Allah sends down rain from the sky and gives life thereby to the earth after its lifelessness. Indeed in that is a sign for a people who listen.'
And this confirms the reality of the believing philosophy upon which Islamic education is based in its cognitive theory.
Among the objectives of the verses of the horizons:
As for the ultimate goal behind all of this, it is reaching the Quranic truth: '... until it becomes clear to them that it is the truth' [Fussilat 41:53]. And knowing His signs: 'And say, Praise to Allah. He will show you His signs, and you will recognize them' [An-Naml 27:93]. And this falls within the framework of the general objectives of the theory of knowledge in the Quran and its educational implications.
As for the subsidiary objectives, we suffice here to indicate that the Quran, when it pays attention to the verses of the horizons related to the exercise of the powers of the intellect, for example, it clearly calls man to learn by observing things, and his practical experience in life, and by interacting with the universe and what it contains of creatures and events, through various sensory or rational methods.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition on the Quranic concept of 'ayat al-afaq' (cosmic signs) and their role in knowledge acquisition and education. The author begins by stating that educationally, this concept makes the 'field of horizons' a primary source of cognitive content, providing knowledge of laws and theories derived from nature. The verses of the horizons—those related to astronomy, day and night, sun and moon—are presented as functional, each with defined roles, all harmonizing with their Creator. This harmony serves an educational purpose: the content is not mere information but is practical, with functional objectives. The author then cites Quranic verses (Yunus 10:5 and 10:67) as examples, showing how these signs teach calculation and provide rest and sight. The harmony between creation and Creator leads the intellect to benefit from all elements, achieving the subjugation (taskhir) of the universe for humanity, which is part of the 'world of witnessing' (al-shahada). This applies to both celestial and earthly phenomena, as illustrated by verses from al-Baqarah, al-Hajj, and al-Nahl, which speak of creation, subjugation, and provision. The author then states that this confirms the 'believing philosophy' underlying Islamic education. Next, the ultimate objective is identified: arriving at the Quranic truth (Fussilat 41:53) and recognizing Allah's signs (al-Naml 27:93), which are general goals of the Quranic theory of knowledge. Subsidiary objectives include the Quran's call to learn through observation, practical experience, and interaction with the universe via sensory and rational methods. The passage thus establishes the epistemic and educational framework where the universe is both a source and a sign, with clear teleological aims.

Key Terms
آيات الآفاق
ميدان المعرفة
وظيفية المحتوى
تسخير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the 'verses of the horizons' and the Creator?
A) They are independent and self-sufficient.
B) They exist in harmony with their Creator, affirming their subordination to Him.
C) They are in conflict with divine will.
D) They are merely decorative.

Key Takeaway
The cosmic signs are not neutral facts; they are functional revelations that, when observed, lead to knowledge of Allah and serve human benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Using the passage as a guide, identify two examples of Ayat al-Afaq from the verses cited (Yunus 10:5 and 10:67) and explain how each serves both a practical purpose (e.g., telling time) and a spiritual purpose (pointing to the Creator).
?
2. Discuss how the concept of 'wazifiyyat al-muhtawa' (functionality of content) would apply to the study of astronomy in an Islamic curriculum: what functional objectives does such study serve?

intermediate
7 min
The Educational Objectives of Cosmic Signs: from Awareness to Worship
Author explains the role of cosmic signs in Islamic epistemology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ultimate and subsidiary educational objectives of studying Ayat al-Afaq as outlined in the Quran.

Core Idea
The ultimate goal of studying the cosmos is to recognize that the Quran is the truth and to know Allah.

The passage does not stop at describing cosmic signs as knowledge sources; it also specifies the aims. The ultimate aim is 'reaching the Quranic truth' and 'knowing His signs'. Subsidiary aims include learning through observation and experience. This lesson breaks down these objectives and shows how they align with Islamic educational theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ultimate goal
Find the verses quoted: 'until it becomes clear to them that it is the truth' (Fussilat 41:53) and 'He will show you His signs, and you will recognize them' (An-Naml 27:93). Recognize that the purpose transcends mere empirical accumulation.
2
Identify the subsidiary objectives
The passage says the Quran calls to 'learning by observing things, practical experience, and interaction with the universe through sensory or rational methods.' These are the immediate methods.
3
Understand the connection
The subsidiary objectives serve the ultimate goal. The functional nature of cosmic content is designed to lead to faith and recognition of Allah.
