Distinguishing Tadafu' from Sira'
Author critiques clash of civilizations and introduces tadafu' as pluralism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'al-tadafu' (mutual repulsion) and 'al-sira' (conflict) as presented in the Quranic framework, and explain why the clash of civilizations thesis is incompatible with Islamic teachings.

Core Idea
Tadafu' is pluralism, not conflict; Islam affirms unity of creation and mutual recognition.

The author critiques Western theses that portray Islam as a challenge or that predict an inevitable clash. He counters by presenting an Islamic view based on the verse 'We made you into nations and tribes that you may know one another' (Q. 49:13). The key is understanding the Quranic concept of 'tadafu'' – a dynamic interaction that is not hostile but pluralistic. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Western theses criticized
Find where the author mentions Huntington's 'clash of civilizations' and Fukuyama's 'end of history' in the Arabic passage. Note how he critiques their motivations (e.g., incitement against Muslims).
Huntington and Fukuyama are mentioned by name in the passage.
2
Extract the Islamic objection
Look for the sentence that says the clash thesis is an 'illusion' and that Islam is based on 'unity of creation'. Identify the Quranic principle cited: mutual recognition (ta'aruf) not conflict.
The passage mentions that Islam recognizes Jews, Christians, Sabians, and Magians as People of the Dhimma.
3
Distinguish tadafu' from sira'
Find the researcher's distinction: tadafu' is 'ta'addudiyya' (pluralism) while sira' is hostile opposition. Understand that tadafu' is a sunna (divine law) that allows coexistence and a common ground in neutral sciences.
The Arabic text states: 'التدافع تعددية' (al-tadafu' is pluralism).
4
Recognize the principle of ta'aruf
Connect the author's claim that Islam calls for mutual recognition (ta'aruf) to the Quranic verse implicit in the passage. Reflect on how this differs from both conflict and forced uniformity.
Ta'aruf is derived from the same root as 'arafa (to know), implying respectful interaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
وهو المعتقدات الدينية. وقد أفصح عن ذلك في حوار أجرته معه مجلة التايم الأمريكية حيث صرّح أن الإسلام هو التحدي الأكثر صراحة في هذا العالم). وكذلك حاول (فوكوياما) أن يصنف كتاباً في نهاية التاريخ. ومع أن (فوكوياما) أمريكي الجنسية لكنه ياباني الأصل، ولذلك فكأنه يحاول الاعتذار لأمريكا عما فعلته بشعبه في هيروشيما و ناجازاكي فراح يدعي أن نهاية التاريخ سيعلن عنها عند قمة تطور الحضارة الغربية(٢).
والغرض من ذلك كله استعداء الغرب والعالم على المسلمين، وعدم السماح الحضارتهم بأن تزيح عن كاهلها موروث التخلف والجهل الذي أسهمت الدول الاستعمارية الغربية بقسط وافر في حلوله وترسيخه.
ويرى بعض الباحثين أن موضوع صدام الحضارات وهم من أساسه بالنسبة إلى نظرة الإسلام وأنه ينبغي أن يعرف الغرب أن الإسلام السوي قائم على تقرير وحدة الخلق بين بني الإنسان مهما اختلفت معتقداتهم الدينية أو ألوانهم أو أجناسهم أو ثقافاتهم، إذ إن ذلك لا يمثل أكثر من مظهر سنني، في إطار سنن الله في الوجود، بهدف التعارف لا التعارك. وقد وجه الإسلام أتباعه إلى الاعتراف بأديان الآخرين يهوداً كانوا أم نصارى، بل واستوعب حتى الصابئة والمجوس، واعتبرهم أهل ذمة، داعياً الجميع إلى عدم التنازع في هذا لأمر، فذلك مما يختص الله به يوم الحساب. يحارب الإسلام القهر والعدوان والهيمنة السياسية للغرب التي تقوم على أساس من سيادة الرجل الأبيض(۳).
وهنا قد يُشكل هذا المفهوم إذا ما تم تبنيه في إطار سنة التدافع، من حيث إنه إقرار بحتمية هذه السنة بوجه من الوجوه.
ويجيب أحد الباحثين على ذلك بتفريقه بين الصراع والتدافع، إذ التدافع تعددية، والتعددية هي السنة اللازبة والإسلام مع التعددية، ومع تعايش الحضارات، وبذلك فيمكن أن يكون هناك قاسم مشترك بين الإنسانية يتمثل في العلوم الطبيعية المحايدة، في حين تتمايز الحضارات في الفلسفات (۱).
ويذهب باحث آخر إلى أبعد من ذلك حيث يستخلص من فكرة ختم النبوة انتهاء فكرة الدورات الحضارية، التي تعني ولادتها ضعيفة، ثم تقوى وتشتد، ثم تضعف وتزول. ولكن لما كان الفارق الجوهري بين الإنسان والحضارة هو أن الإنسان قد يمرض فتتعرض حياته العضوية للتحلل، أما الحضارة فإن أصابها المرض فتحللها فكري نفسي، وهذا قابل للعلاج والزيادة والنمو. ولذلك فإن أرنولد توينبي) حينما تناول هذا الموضوع لم يحسم الأمر بانتهاء دورة حضارية لتحل أخرى محلّها، ولكنه تناول الأمر بقدر من التردد. ويختم هذا الباحث وجهة نظره بالتأكيد على أن فكرة ختم النبوة بالنسبة للرسول محمد - - للناس كافة؛ تعني إمكان إحلال فكرة عالمية الحضارة، وانتهاء زمن تعدد الحضارات. ومع أننا ما نزال نعيش دورة الحضارة وتعددها إلا أن إرهاصات زوالها بدأت تبرز لمن تأمل (٢). ولعلّ الرأي الذي أخلص إليه بعد كل ما تقدّم أنه يجب التفريق بين مستويين من خطاب القرآن لمظهر التدافع الحضاري وذلك على النحو التالي:
المستوى الأول: خطاب القرآن عن نظرته الذاتية إلى هذه السنة من منطلق الاعتراف الكامل بذاتية الآخر، وكينونته المستقلة، وحقه في إقامة الحضارة التي يتمحض اختياره المطلق في إقامتها، شريطة عدم تعديها لحدودها، أو تجاوزها
Chapter Two: Section Two - Field of Knowledge - the Unseen and the Witnessed. It is religious beliefs. He has expressed that in an interview conducted with him by Time magazine where he stated that Islam is the most blunt challenge in this world. Likewise, (Fukuyama) tried to write a book on the end of history. Although (Fukuyama) is American by nationality, he is of Japanese origin, and therefore it is as if he is trying to apologize to America for what it did to his people in Hiroshima and Nagasaki, so he claimed that the end of history would be announced at the peak of the development of Western civilization (2). The purpose of all that is to incite the West and the world against Muslims, and not to allow their civilization to shed from its shoulders the inherited backwardness and ignorance to which the Western colonial states contributed a large share in its dissemination and consolidation. Some researchers see that the topic of the clash of civilizations is an illusion from its foundation from the perspective of Islam, and that the West should know that sound Islam is based on affirming the unity of creation among human beings regardless of their religious beliefs, colors, races, or cultures, for that represents no more than a natural phenomenon, within the framework of God's laws in existence, for the purpose of mutual recognition, not conflict. Islam has directed its followers to recognize the religions of others, whether they are Jews or Christians, and even accommodated the Sabians and Magians, and considered them People of the Dhimma, calling everyone to not dispute in this matter, for that is what God alone will judge on the Day of Reckoning. Islam fights oppression, aggression, and the political hegemony of the West based on the supremacy of the white man (3). Here, this concept may be problematic if adopted within the framework of the sunna of mutual repulsion (tadafu'), insofar as it is an acknowledgment of the inevitability of this sunna in some way. One researcher responds to that by distinguishing between conflict and mutual repulsion (tadafu'), for mutual repulsion is pluralism, and pluralism is the eternal sunna, and Islam is with pluralism, and with the coexistence of civilizations, and thus there can be a common denominator among humanity represented by neutral natural sciences, while civilizations differ in philosophies (1). Another researcher goes further by deducing from the idea of the seal of prophethood the end of the idea of civilizational cycles, which means they are born weak, then grow strong and intensify, then weaken and disappear. But because the essential difference between man and civilization is that man may become sick thus his organic life is subject to decomposition, whereas if civilization is afflicted with illness, its decomposition is intellectual-psychological, and this is subject to treatment, increase, and growth. Therefore, when Arnold Toynbee addressed this topic, he did not settle the matter with the end of one civilizational cycle to be replaced by another, but he addressed it with a degree of hesitation. This researcher concludes his view by affirming that the idea of the seal of prophethood for the Messenger Muhammad - peace be upon him - for all people means the possibility of establishing the idea of the universality of civilization, and the end of the time of multiple civilizations. Although we still live in the cycle of civilization and its multiplicity, the harbingers of its demise have begun to appear for those who reflect (2). Perhaps the opinion I conclude with after all that is that a distinction must be made between two levels of the Quranic discourse regarding the manifestation of civilizational mutual repulsion, as follows: The first level: The Quran's discourse about its subjective view of this sunna from the standpoint of full recognition of the other's subjectivity, his independent existence, and his right to establish the civilization that his absolute choice chooses to establish, provided it does not transgress its limits or exceed them
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion of the concept of civilizational interaction from an Islamic perspective, critiquing the Western thesis of a 'clash of civilizations' as promoted by Huntington and Fukuyama. The author begins by stating that the field of knowledge includes the unseen and the witnessed, which are religious beliefs. He then cites Huntington's claim that Islam is the most blunt challenge, and Fukuyama's thesis on the end of history, suggesting that Fukuyama's Japanese origin makes his apology for American actions in Hiroshima and Nagasaki suspect. The author argues that the purpose of these theses is to incite the West against Muslims and prevent Islamic civilization from overcoming its inherited backwardness, to which colonialism contributed. He then presents the view of some researchers that the clash of civilizations is an illusion from Islam's standpoint, because Islam affirms the unity of creation and recognizes other religions, including Jews, Christians, Sabians, and Magians as People of the Dhimma, and promotes mutual recognition (ta'aruf) rather than conflict (ta'aruk). However, this view might be problematic if adopted within the framework of the sunna of 'tadafu'' (mutual repulsion), as it would seem to endorse a deterministic conflict. A researcher responds by distinguishing between conflict (sira') and tadafu', where tadafu' is understood as pluralism (ta'addudiyya) and coexistence, allowing for a common ground in neutral sciences while civilizations differ in philosophies. Another researcher goes further by linking the seal of prophethood (khatm al-nubuwwa) to the end of civilizational cycles. He argues that while individuals age and die, civilizations can be treated and renewed, so the cyclic view is not absolute. Toynbee himself was hesitant. The conclusion is that the seal of prophethood implies the possibility of a universal civilization, ending the era of multiple civilizations. The author then offers his own conclusion: a distinction must be made between two levels of Quranic discourse on civilizational tadafu': the first level recognizes the other's subjectivity and right to establish their own civilization, provided they do not transgress limits. The passage thus refines the concept of tadafu' by distinguishing it from conflict and linking it to Islamic principles of pluralism and the universal message of Prophet Muhammad.

Key Terms
التدافع
الصراع
التعددية
التعارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does one researcher distinguish between 'sira' (conflict) and 'tadafu' (mutual repulsion)?
A) Conflict is inevitable while tadafu' is avoidable.
B) Tadafu' is pluralism and coexistence, while conflict is opposition.
C) Both are the same but with different names.
D) Tadafu' is a form of conflict that leads to war.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic concept of tadafu' must be understood as a pluralistic divine sunna that allows for coexistence, not as a justification for conflict.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a contemporary interaction between two Muslim-majority societies (e.g., economic cooperation, cultural exchange) and analyze whether it fits tadafu' (pluralistic interaction) or sira' (conflict) based on the criteria in the passage.
?
Construct an argument from the passage that would refute a claim that Islam inherently clashes with Western civilization, using the distinction between tadafu' and sira'.

Seal of Prophethood and Civilizational Universality
Author presents a researcher's argument linking khatm al-nubuwwa to civilizational cycles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the argument that the seal of prophethood (khatm al-nubuwwa) implies the end of civilizational cycles and the possibility of a universal civilization.

Core Idea
Khatm al-nubuwwa transforms civilization from mortal cycle to treatable and universalizable entity.

Building on the previous distinction between tadafu' and conflict, the author introduces another researcher's innovative link between the Islamic doctrine of khatm al-nubuwwa and the philosophy of history. If Prophet Muhammad is the final prophet for all humanity, perhaps the cyclical rise and fall of civilizations can be overcome. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Recall the doctrine of Khatm al-Nubuwwa
Khatm al-nubuwwa means that Prophet Muhammad is the last prophet, and his message is universal for all humanity until the Day of Judgment. This is a core Islamic belief.
You should already know this; the passage assumes it.
2
Understand the cyclical view of civilizations
The author mentions the idea of civilizational cycles (birth, strength, weakness, disappearance). This is associated with historians like Ibn Khaldun and Toynbee. The cycle seems inevitable.
The passage specifically refers to Arnold Toynbee and his hesitation about strict cycles.
3
Follow the researcher's argument
The researcher argues that the essential difference between human and civilization is that humans die biologically, but civilizations are intellectual-psychological constructs that can be treated and renewed. Therefore, the cyclical model is not absolute, especially in light of khatm al-nubuwwa, which suggests the possibility of a universal civilization ending the cycle of multiple civilizations.
The Arabic text says: 'ولما كان الفارق الجوهري بين الإنسان والحضارة هو أن الإنسان قد يمرض فتتعرض حياته العضوية للتحلل، أما الحضارة فإن أصابها المرض فتحللها فكري نفسي، وهذا قابل للعلاج'.
4
Evaluate the implications
The researcher concludes that khatm al-nubuwwa opens the door to a universal civilization. Although we still experience multiple civilizations, signs of the old cycle's end are appearing. Consider how this connects to the Islamic eschatological vision.
The author does not fully endorse this view but presents it as a significant perspective.

الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
وهو المعتقدات الدينية. وقد أفصح عن ذلك في حوار أجرته معه مجلة التايم الأمريكية حيث صرّح أن الإسلام هو التحدي الأكثر صراحة في هذا العالم). وكذلك حاول (فوكوياما) أن يصنف كتاباً في نهاية التاريخ. ومع أن (فوكوياما) أمريكي الجنسية لكنه ياباني الأصل، ولذلك فكأنه يحاول الاعتذار لأمريكا عما فعلته بشعبه في هيروشيما و ناجازاكي فراح يدعي أن نهاية التاريخ سيعلن عنها عند قمة تطور الحضارة الغربية(٢).
والغرض من ذلك كله استعداء الغرب والعالم على المسلمين، وعدم السماح الحضارتهم بأن تزيح عن كاهلها موروث التخلف والجهل الذي أسهمت الدول الاستعمارية الغربية بقسط وافر في حلوله وترسيخه.
ويرى بعض الباحثين أن موضوع صدام الحضارات وهم من أساسه بالنسبة إلى نظرة الإسلام وأنه ينبغي أن يعرف الغرب أن الإسلام السوي قائم على تقرير وحدة الخلق بين بني الإنسان مهما اختلفت معتقداتهم الدينية أو ألوانهم أو أجناسهم أو ثقافاتهم، إذ إن ذلك لا يمثل أكثر من مظهر سنني، في إطار سنن الله في الوجود، بهدف التعارف لا التعارك. وقد وجه الإسلام أتباعه إلى الاعتراف بأديان الآخرين يهوداً كانوا أم نصارى، بل واستوعب حتى الصابئة والمجوس، واعتبرهم أهل ذمة، داعياً الجميع إلى عدم التنازع في هذا لأمر، فذلك مما يختص الله به يوم الحساب. يحارب الإسلام القهر والعدوان والهيمنة السياسية للغرب التي تقوم على أساس من سيادة الرجل الأبيض(۳).
وهنا قد يُشكل هذا المفهوم إذا ما تم تبنيه في إطار سنة التدافع، من حيث إنه إقرار بحتمية هذه السنة بوجه من الوجوه.

According to the passage, what is the essential difference between humans and civilizations that the researcher uses to argue against inevitable cycles?

Quranic Defensive Struggle and the Concept of Ḥirābah
Author explains Quran's stance on the other and the concept of ḥirābah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Quranic defensive struggle (ḥirābah) from the aim of eliminating disbelief and explain the two levels of Quranic discourse about the other.

Core Idea
The Quran's struggle is defensive (ḥirābah), not elimination; the other is warned but not universally condemned.

This passage clarifies the Quran's stance on dealing with those who oppose Islam. It emphasizes that the conflict is not about eradicating disbelief but about repelling aggression—a concept known juristically as ḥirābah. The author then distinguishes two levels of Quranic discourse: one defining the defensive struggle, and another characterizing the other's persistent attempts to seduce Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two levels of discourse
Locate where the author introduces 'المستوى الأول' (the first level) and 'المستوى الآخر' (the other level). The first level defines the nature of struggle; the second level describes the other's behavior.
2
Extract the definition of ḥirābah
Find the sentence stating that the conflict is 'ليس بهدف القضاء على هذا الكفر، وإنما بهدف ردّ العدوان'. Note that this is the juristic term for repelling aggression.
The term 'الحرابة' is used in fiqh for fighting against those who threaten safety.
3
Note restrictions on the second level
The author says it is restricted to a specific group (فريق من الكافرين) and time (زمن النبي). Understand that this does not apply universally.
4
Understand the shift in Islamic education
The passage describes a shift from coexistence to contestation when hegemonic ideologies like pragmatism arise. Identify the two reasons given: cultural dominance of modern education and psychological defeat of the elite.

في هذا المستوى من الخطاب يتحدد موقف القرآن من الآخر على نحو جليّ من خلال تلك الآيات التي أوضحت أن صراع الإسلام مع الكفر ليس بهدف القضاء على هذا الكفر، وإنما بهدف ردّ العدوان الذي يُهدِّدُ به معسكر الكفر، فيما يسمى فقهياً بالحرابة. وقد أكد هذا موقف الإسلام العملي من خلال دعوة النبي - صلى الله عليه وسلم – في مختلف أطوارها. يعني المستوى الآخر: خطاب القرآن الإخباري عن الآخر في حرصه على إغواء المسلمين بشتى الوسائل، وإصراره على ذلك. ولكن هذا مقيد بفريق من الكافرين، أو حتى بجملة الكافرين من أهل الكتاب على وجه التحديد في زمن النبي - - دون أن يعني ذلك استغراقاً لكل المخالفين بالضرورة، ودون أن ذلك موقفاً يرتضيه الإسلام كذلك. فكأن الإسلام – بعد أن حدد موقفه من قضية التدافع الحضاري في المستوى الأول – يومى بأن الآخر يختلف عنـه في الموقف ذاته، ولذلك فإن صح أن تتحتم فكرة المدافعة الحضارية فإن المتسبب الأوحد فيها هو الطرف الآخر، لا الإسلام، وبناءً على هذا الاستخلاص فإن التربية الإسلامية لا تقف من الأفكار والاتجاهات موقف المناهض، وإنما موقف الندّ المتفاعل، ولكن حين تسعى بعض تلك الأفكار والاتجاهات الغربية - مثلاً - إلى الهيمنة ومحاولة بسط النفوذ على ما عداها من النظريات والأفكار والاتجاهات الأخرى، كما هو حال ما يسمى اليوم بالتربية الحديثة التربية البراجماتية) بحجة أن ما عداها رجعية وطوباوية عتيقة، حينئذ ينتقل موقف التربية الإسلامية من وضعية الإقرار والتعايش مع الآخر إلى موقف المنازع حول الأحقية والمشروعية وسمة العالمية. وهذا ما يفترض أن يكون انعكاسه واضحاً مباشراً عبر الفلسفة التربوية الموجهة للنظام التربوي بكل عناصره في المجتمع المسلم. ويبدو أن غياب فلسفة التربية الإسلامية عن ميدان التنافس المتكافئ يرجع إلى سببين رئيسين: الأول: سيادة الفعل الثقافي والحضاري لمن يتبنى ما يسمى بـ (التربية الحديثة) أو البراجماتية. الثاني: الهزيمة النفسية التي لحقت النخبة الفلسفية منذ مطلع القرن العشرين الميلادي. وطريق التدافع هو بلورة التكتل الإسلامي في عالم التكتلات العالمية المتنافسة على السيادة. ومن خلاله يمكن أن يقرأ الآخرون معالم الفلسفة ومخرجاتها، والمسلمون في مركز القوة.
At this level of discourse, the Quran's stance towards the other is clearly determined through those verses which made clear that the conflict of Islam with disbelief is not for the purpose of eliminating this disbelief, but rather for the purpose of repelling the aggression that the camp of disbelief threatens with, in what is juristically called al-ḥirābah. This was confirmed by the practical stance of Islam through the call of the Prophet - may God bless him and grant him peace - in its various stages. The other level: the Quran's informational discourse about the other in his eagerness to seduce Muslims by various means, and his insistence on that. But this is restricted to a group of the disbelievers, or even to the entirety of the disbelievers from the People of the Book specifically in the time of the Prophet, without that necessarily implying encompassment of all opponents, and without that being a stance that Islam approves as well. It is as if Islam - after determining its stance on the issue of civilizational conflict in the first level - indicates that the other differs from it in the same stance, and therefore if the idea of civilizational conflict becomes inevitable, the sole cause of it is the other party, not Islam. Based on this conclusion, Islamic education does not adopt a stance of opposition towards ideas and trends, but rather a stance of an interactive equal. But when some of those Western ideas and trends - for example - seek hegemony and attempt to extend influence over other theories, ideas, and trends, as is the case with what is today called modern education (pragmatic education) under the pretext that what is other than it is reactionary and outdated utopianism, then the stance of Islamic education shifts from a position of acknowledgment and coexistence with the other to a position of contestation over entitlement, legitimacy, and the attribute of universality. This is supposed to be clearly and directly reflected through the educational philosophy guiding the educational system with all its elements in Muslim society. It appears that the absence of Islamic educational philosophy from the field of equal competition is due to two main reasons: First: the dominance of the cultural and civilizational activity of those who adopt what is called (modern education) or pragmatism. Second: the psychological defeat that befell the philosophical elite since the beginning of the twentieth century CE. The way of conflict is the crystallization of the Islamic bloc in a world of competing global blocs over sovereignty. Through it, others can read the features of the philosophy and its outputs, with Muslims in a position of strength.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage explains the Quran's discourse regarding the 'other' (al-ākhar), primarily focusing on two levels. At the first level, the Quran clarifies that the struggle between Islam and disbelief is fundamentally defensive, not aimed at eradication but at repelling aggression, termed juristically as al-ḥirābah. This is supported by the practical example of the Prophet's call in its various stages. The second level deals with the informational discourse warning about the other's persistent attempts to seduce Muslims, but this is contextually restricted to specific groups, such as certain disbelievers or the People of the Book during the Prophet's time, and does not encompass all opponents globally or permanently. The passage then addresses the shift in Islamic education's stance: initially interactive and equal, but when faced with hegemonic Western ideologies like pragmatism that dismiss others as backward, Islamic education must contest for legitimacy and universality. The author identifies two reasons for the absence of Islamic educational philosophy in fair competition: cultural dominance of modern education and psychological defeat of the philosophical elite since the early 20th century. The resolution proposed is to form a strong Islamic bloc within global competing blocs, enabling others to recognize its philosophy while Muslims are in a position of strength.

Key Terms
الحرابة
التدافع الحضاري
التربية البراجماتية

Checkpoint

A) To eliminate disbelief entirely
B) To repel aggression threatening from the camp of disbelief
C) To convert all people to Islam by force
D) To establish a global caliphate

Key Takeaway
The Quranic approach to the other is defensive (ḥirābah) and context-specific, not a universal call to eliminate all opponents.

Al-Ibtilā' as a Universal Sunnah in the Quran
Author presents the Quranic concept of al-ibtilā' as a universal sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Quranic foundations for the concept of al-ibtilā' and explain how it applies to believers as a universal sunnah.

Core Idea
Testing (ibtilā') is a universal sunnah, not punishment, but a means to distinguish excellence in deeds.

Divine testing is often misunderstood as mere punishment. In this passage, the author reveals that testing is a sunnah (divine practice) woven into creation itself—from the moment God's Throne was upon water—and continues through the histories of all nations, including the early Muslim community at Uhud. By examining the Quranic foundations, we see that ibtilā' is a tool for distinguishing the best in deeds, not a sign of divine displeasure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two foundations of ibtilā'
Read the opening lines: the first foundation goes back to 'distant history when the Throne was upon water'; the second to 'recent history' of the Prophet. Locate these two timeframes in the passage.
The first foundation is cosmic (creation), the second is communal (previous and early Muslim communities).
2
Extract the Quranic evidence for each foundation
The author cites Q. 11:7 for the first foundation, and Q. 2:214 for the second. Write down the verses and note their key phrases: 'that He might test you' (Q. 11:7) and 'the likes of those who passed away before you were touched by poverty and hardship' (Q. 2:214).
The verse for the battle of Uhud (Q. 3:152) is given as a specific application.
3
Understand the purpose of testing from the passage
The purpose is stated in Q. 11:7: 'that He might test you as to which of you is best in deed.' Also, the test at Uhud reveals who desires the world vs. the hereafter. Testing distinguishes sincerity and refines faith.
Testing is not punitive but evaluative and pedagogical.
4
Apply the concept to the early Muslim community
The passage explicitly states that the 'unique Quranic generation' was tested at Uhud due to their own shortcomings. This shows ibtilā' applies to even the best of communities.
The test includes forgiveness—'He has forgiven you'—reinforcing it as a mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمة أساسان لمظهر الابتلاء يرجع أحدهما للتاريخ البعيد حيث كان العرش على الماء، وذلك ما أشار إليه القرآن فقال: وَهُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضَ فِي سِتَّةِ أَيَّامٍ وَكَانَ عَرْشُهُ عَلَى الْماءِ لِيَبْلُوَكُمْ أَيُّكُمْ أَحْسَنُ عَمَلاً [مود: ۷/۱۱]. الآخر إلى التاريخ القريب بالنسبة للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم- ويرجع وتلك هي إشارة القرآن في قوله : أَمْ حَسِبْتُمْ أَن تَدْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ وَلَمَا يَأْتِكُمْ مَثَلُ الَّذِينَ خَلَوْا مِنْ قَبْلِكُمْ مَسَّتْهُمُ الْبَأْسَاءُ وَالضَّرَاءُ وَزُلْزِلُوا حَتَّى يَقُولَ الرَّسُولُ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مَعَهُ مَتَى نَصْرُ اللَّهِ أَلا إِنَّ نَصْرَ اللَّهِ قَرِيبٌ) [البقرة: ٢١٤/٢] وفي ضوء هذا فإن الابتلاء سنة ماضية بين الأمم، بمن في ذلك المسلمون الذين يوصفون بالجيل القرآني الفريد فقد ابتلوا بهزيمة معركة أحد على الرغم من الأسباب الموضوعية التي تعود إلى تقصيرهم ومخالفتهم: ﴿وَلَقَدْ صَدَقَكُمُ اللهُ وَعْدَهُ إِذْ تَحُسُّونَهُمْ بِإِذْنِهِ حَتَّى إذا فَشِلْتُمْ وَتَنَازَعْتُمْ فِي الأَمْرِ وَعَصَيْتُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا أَرَاكُمْ ما تُحِبُّونَ مِنْكُمْ مَنْ يُرِيدُ الدُّنْيا وَمِنْكُمْ مَنْ يُرِيدُ الآخِرَةَ ثُمَّ صَرَفَكُمْ عَنْهُمْ لِيَبْتَلِيَكُمْ وَلَقَدْ عَفَا عَنْكُمْ وَاللَّهُ ذُو فَضْلٍ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ) [آل عمران: ١٥٢/٣].
There are two foundations for the manifestation of testing, one of which goes back to the distant history when the Throne was upon the water, as indicated by the Quran when He said: 'And it is He who created the heavens and the earth in six days, and His Throne had been upon the water, that He might test you as to which of you is best in deed.' [Hud 11:7]. The other goes back to recent history relative to the Messenger - may God bless him and grant him peace - and that is the indication of the Quran in His saying: 'Or do you think that you will enter Paradise while there has not yet come to you the likes of those who passed away before you? They were touched by poverty and hardship and were shaken until the Messenger and those who believed with him said, "When is the help of God?" Unquestionably, the help of God is near.' [Al-Baqarah 2:214]. In light of this, testing is an ongoing sunnah among the nations, including the Muslims who are described as the unique Quranic generation; they were tested with the defeat of the battle of Uhud despite the objective reasons due to their negligence and disobedience: 'And indeed God fulfilled His promise to you when you were killing them by His permission until you lost courage and disputed about the matter and disobeyed after He had shown you what you love. Among you are those who desire the world, and among you are those who desire the hereafter. Then He turned you away from them that He might test you. And He has forgiven you, and God is full of favor to the believers.' [Al-Imran 3:152].
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of al-ibtilā' (testing or trial) in the Quran, establishing it as a sunnah (divine practice) that applies universally across nations. The author identifies two foundational bases: one from remote history, citing Q. 11:7, where God created the heavens and earth while His Throne was upon water, specifically to test humans regarding their deeds. The second basis is from the near history of the Prophet Muhammad, quoting Q. 2:214, which reminds believers that they cannot expect to enter Paradise without undergoing trials similar to those of previous communities, including hardship and shaking until they cry for divine help. The author then applies this sunnah to the early Muslim community, specifically the 'unique Quranic generation,' who experienced defeat at the Battle of Uhud. This defeat was due to their own shortcomings—faltering, disputing, and disobeying orders—and God turned the enemy upon them as a test. However, He also forgave them, showing His favor. Thus, testing is not limited to non-believers but includes believers as a means of distinguishing the sincere and refining faith.

Key Terms
الابتلاء
العرش
الجيل القرآني الفريد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two historical foundations are given for the concept of testing?
A) The creation of the heavens and earth and the Battle of Badr
B) The Throne upon water and the trials of the Muslim community at Uhud
C) The flood of Noah and the destruction of Thamud
D) The migration to Abyssinia and the conquest of Mecca

Key Takeaway
Al-ibtilā' is a universal sunnah with two Quranic foundations: the primordial test at creation and the historical test of all prophetic communities, including the early Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read Q. 2:214 and Q. 3:152. Explain in your own words how these verses demonstrate the sunnah of testing, using the two foundations from the passage.
?
Write a brief response to someone who claims that the defeat at Uhud was a punishment from God. Use the passage to argue that it was a test, and point to the verse that mentions forgiveness.

The Quranic Concept of Trial: Foundations, Forms, and Purpose
Author discusses the two foundations of trial and its purpose in distinguishing believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two foundations of trial according to the Quran and explain its purpose as discrimination and purification of believers.

Core Idea
Trial encompasses both good and evil to purify believers and reveal their true character.

Many assume trial (ibtila') means only hardship and punishment. Yet the Quran presents trial as a comprehensive divine practice that includes blessings as well as afflictions. Understanding its true scope is essential for grasping the Quranic worldview and its implications for personal development and education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two foundations of trial
Find in the passage the two temporal foundations the author mentions: one goes back to the creation of the heavens and earth (Hud 11:7), the other to the historical trials of previous nations (Baqarah 2:214). These show trial is built into creation and history.
The first foundation is universal and primordial; the second is specific to human communities.
2
List the forms of trial
The author enumerates several forms: trial in wealth, in oneself, and through harm from others (Aal-e-Imran 3:186). Also note that trial includes both evil and good (Al-Anbiya 21:35). Contrast this with the common view that trial is only evil.
All forms occur on earth, the field of trial (Al-Kahf 18:7).
3
Extract the purpose of trial
The passage states the goal is 'discrimination and purification' (tamyeez wa tamhees) of believers from others (Aal-e-Imran 3:141-142). Trial also tests patience and striving, revealing who truly strives and is patient.
The purpose is educational and selective, not punitive.
4
Apply to educational objectives
The author concludes that curriculum should produce a learner aware of this sunna, patient and persevering, able to continue his role despite obstacles. Reflect on how this principle can shape Islamic education.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمة أساسان لمظهر الابتلاء يرجع أحدهما للتاريخ البعيد حيث كان العرش على الماء، وذلك ما أشار إليه القرآن فقال: (وَهُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّماواتِ وَالْأَرْضَ فِي سِتَّةِ أَيَّامٍ وَكَانَ عَرْشُهُ عَلَى الْماءِ لِيَبْلُوَكُمْ أَيُّكُمْ أَحْسَنُ عَمَلاً) [هود: 7/11]. الآخر إلى التاريخ القريب بالنسبة للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم- ويرجع وتلك هي إشارة القرآن في قوله: (أَمْ حَسِبْتُمْ أَن تَدْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ وَلَمَا يَأْتِكُمْ مَثَلُ الَّذِينَ خَلَوْا مِنْ قَبْلِكُمْ مَسَّتْهُمُ الْبَأْسَاءُ وَالضَّرَاءُ وَزُلْزِلُوا حَتَّى يَقُولَ الرَّسُولُ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مَعَهُ مَتَى نَصْرُ اللَّهِ أَلا إِنَّ نَصْرَ اللَّهِ قَرِيبٌ) [البقرة: 214/2]. وفي ضوء هذا فإن الابتلاء سنة ماضية بين الأمم، بمن في ذلك المسلمون الذين يوصفون بالجيل القرآني الفريد فقد ابتلوا بهزيمة معركة وهم الأوائل أحد على الرغم من الأسباب الموضوعية التي تعود إلى تقصيرهم ومخالفتهم: (وَلَقَدْ صَدَقَكُمُ اللهُ وَعْدَهُ إِذْ تَحُسُّونَهُمْ بِإِذْنِهِ حَتَّى إذا فَشِلْتُمْ وَتَنَازَعْتُمْ فِي الأَمْرِ وَعَصَيْتُمْ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا أَرَاكُمْ ما تُحِبُّونَ مِنْكُمْ مَنْ يُرِيدُ الدُّنْيا وَمِنْكُمْ مَنْ يُرِيدُ الآخِرَةَ ثُمَّ صَرَفَكُمْ عَنْهُمْ لِيَبْتَلِيَكُمْ وَلَقَدْ عَفَا عَنْكُمْ وَاللَّهُ ذُو فَضْلٍ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ) [آل عمران: 152/3]. والمظهر الابتلاء صور عدة كالابتلاء في المال والنفس والتعرض لصنوف الأذى من جهات شتى: (لَتُبْلَوُنَّ فِي أَمْوالِكُمْ وَأَنْفُسِكُمْ وَلَتَسْمَعُنَّ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتابَ مِنْ قَبْلِكُمْ وَمِنَ الَّذِينَ أَشْرَكُوا أَذَى كَثِيراً وَإِنْ تَصْبِرُوا وَتَتَّقُوا فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ مِنْ عَزْمِ الأمور) [آل عمران: 186/3]. وجميع صور الابتلاء تتم في ميدان الابتلاء وهو الأرض: (إنا جَعَلْنَا مَا عَلَى الْأَرْضِ زِينَةً لَهَا لِنَبْلُوَهُمْ أَيُّهُمْ أَحْسَنُ عَمَلاً) [الكهف: 7/18]. ويلاحظ أن الابتلاء لا يلزم مظهراً واحداً هو الشر فحسب، بل إن ثمة مظهراً آخر له هو الخير، بما يمثل قسيماً للشر، ولذلك جاء التعبير عنهما في سياق واحد (وَنَبْلُوكُمْ بِالشَّرِّ وَالْخَيْرِ فِتْنَةٌ) [الأنبياء: 35/21]. أما هدف الابتلاء فالتمييز والتمحيص للمؤمنين عمن سواهم، كما يميز المؤمنين في مستويات الصبر على الابتلاء: (وَلِيُمَحِّصَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَيَمْحَقَ الْكَافِرِينَ، أَمْ حَسِبْتُمْ أَنْ تَدْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ وَلَمّا يَعْلَمِ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ جَاهَدُوا مِنْكُمْ وَيَعْلَمَ الصابرين) [آل عمران: 141/3-142]. لذلك كله يجب أن تشمل أهداف المنهج هدف إخراج المتعلم الصابر المثابر المدرك لسنة الابتلاء، كي يقوم بأداء دوره في مجتمعه رغم العوائق المختلفة، ولكنها لن تثنيه عن المضي في طريق الاستخلاف والبناء. كما تشمل سنة الابتلاء: أسلوب التعلم بالحَدَث من خلال المواقف المتعددة، والصور المتنوعة لمظهر الابتلاء.
There are two foundations for the manifestation of trial: one goes back to the distant past when the Throne was upon the water, and that is what the Quran pointed to saying: 'And it is He who created the heavens and the earth in six days, and His Throne had been upon water, that He might test you which of you is best in deed' [Hud 11:7]. The other goes back to the recent past relative to the Messenger, peace be upon him, and that is the Quran's indication in His saying: 'Or do you think that you will enter Paradise while there has not yet come to you the like of those who passed away before you? They were touched by poverty and hardship and were shaken until the Messenger and those who believed with him said, "When is the help of Allah?" Unquestionably, the help of Allah is near' [Al-Baqarah 2:214]. In light of this, trial is an ongoing sunna among nations, including the Muslims who are described as the unique Quranic generation; they were indeed tried with the defeat of the Battle of Uhud despite the objective reasons due to their shortcomings and disobedience: 'And Allah had certainly fulfilled His promise to you when you were killing them by His permission until you lost courage and disputed about the order and disobeyed after He had shown you what you love. Among you are some who desire this world, and among you are some who desire the Hereafter. Then He turned you away from them that He might test you. And He has forgiven you, and Allah is full of favor to the believers' [Aal-e-Imran 3:152]. The manifestation of trial has several forms such as trial in wealth, in oneself, and exposure to various kinds of harm from different directions: 'You will surely be tested in your possessions and in yourselves, and you will surely hear from those who were given the Scripture before you and from those who associate others with Allah much abuse. But if you are patient and fear Allah, indeed that is of the matters of determination' [Aal-e-Imran 3:186]. And all forms of trial take place in the field of trial, which is the earth: 'Indeed, We have made that which is on the earth adornment for it that We may test them as to which of them is best in deed' [Al-Kahf 18:7]. It is observed that trial is not limited to one manifestation which is evil only; rather there is another manifestation of it which is good, representing a counterpart to evil. Therefore, both are expressed in a single context: 'And We test you with evil and with good as trial' [Al-Anbiya 21:35]. As for the goal of trial, it is discrimination and screening of the believers from others, just as it distinguishes the believers in levels of patience under trial: 'And that Allah might purify the believers and destroy the disbelievers. Or do you think that you will enter Paradise while Allah has not yet made evident those who strive among you and made evident those who are patient?' [Aal-e-Imran 3:141-142]. Therefore, the objectives of the curriculum must include the goal of producing a patient, persevering learner who is aware of the sunna of trial, so that he can fulfill his role in his society despite various obstacles, which will not deter him from proceeding on the path of stewardship and construction. And the sunna of trial also includes the method of learning by event through multiple situations and diverse forms of the manifestation of trial.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of trial (ibtila') in the Quranic worldview. The author begins by establishing two foundations for trial: one primordial, when Allah created the heavens and earth while His Throne was on water, indicating that the purpose of creation itself is trial (Hud 11:7). The second foundation is historical, referring to the trials faced by earlier nations as mentioned in Surah Al-Baqarah 2:214, which sets the context for the Muslim community's trials. The author then clarifies that trial is a continuous sunna among nations, citing the Battle of Uhud (Aal-e-Imran 3:152) as an example where Muslims were tested due to their disobedience. The passage enumerates various forms of trial: in wealth, in oneself, and through harm from others (Aal-e-Imran 3:186), and notes that the arena of all trials is the earth (Al-Kahf 18:7). Importantly, trial includes both evil and good (Al-Anbiya 21:35), contrary to a common misconception that trial is only hardship. The ultimate goal of trial is discrimination (tamyeez) and purification (tamhees) of believers from others, and to reveal levels of patience and striving (Aal-e-Imran 3:141-142). The author concludes by applying this to educational objectives: the curriculum must produce a learner who understands the sunna of trial, remains patient, and continues his role despite obstacles. The passage is theological and educational, not logical in the Aristotelian sense, but it uses Quranic evidence to support its claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary goal of trial (ibtila')?
A) Punishment for disobedience
B) Discrimination and purification of believers
C) Increasing worldly wealth
D) Destroying the disbelievers only

Key Takeaway
Trial is a divine sunna with two foundations, encompassing both good and evil, designed to purify believers and reveal their patience and striving.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a Quranic verse (other than those cited) that illustrates one of the forms of trial (e.g., wealth, self, harm). Identify which form it represents and explain how it serves the purpose of discrimination/purification.
?
Reflect on a contemporary situation where Muslims face trial (e.g., financial crisis, persecution, or even prosperity). Using the author's framework, analyze how this situation can be understood as part of the sunna of ibtila' and what educational objective it might fulfill.
